While Yang Xiong lamented the *Beautiful New*.
Laozi’s dark words grew obscure,
Guan Yin knew the pursuit of the mean.
Zhuangzi and Liezi stood as strange masters,
The *Pian Dao* school taught emptiness.
Their doctrines arose amid Zhou’s decline,
Yet how far could their wild defenses go?
If the times favor not the good,
Detachment leads to nothingness.

The supreme Dao wondrously embraces the Three Ultimates,
Human culture reveals the imperial heart.
Benevolence and righteousness are heaven’s nature,
Endowment of essence—why confusion or delusion?
To master reverence is to achieve purity,
In conduct, guard the self with care.
The mean and harmony govern the balance,
Generation and growth reside in the spirit’s work.
Drill and contemplate to grasp the thread,
In subtlety and peril, be steadfast and reverent.
Beware the boastful and obsequious,
Who miss the wind of Lian and Luo.
In secluded integrity, I hold distant longing,
Yet where shall the crooked and devious turn?

Joy in the dwelling of fish and birds,
Harmony in the following of springs and stones.
The vast tune of high antiquity,
Silent and profound, returns to Fuxi and Nong.
Embracing truth, I awaken to suspended liberation,
In *equalizing things*, I probe my own mystery.
The crescent moon foretells the hidden depths,
The compass’s center aligns with the profound abyss.
Vacuity and clarity share the pivot,
Wondrous union intertwines in distant revolution.
Yang fire overflows the true season,
Yin ice melts the cold spring.
The yellow center turns the chariot’s track,
A single breath completes the celestial cycle.
Jade liquid nurtures the spirit root,
Jasper radiance blooms in the field of mushrooms.
Divine transformation defies verbal measure,
Its signs vast as the dark expanse.

Long have I tasted the secrets of the mysterious mandate,
Riding the wind to summon the immortal Gu Quan.
Supreme harmony lies in preserving union,
Guiding the reins to soar on high.
Sitting in forgetfulness, the swallow rests at ease,
While the shallow world entangles in frantic pursuit.
If one truly understands the principle of life,
The nature and destiny of things become utterly clear.
No need to wield the blade in idle play,
The sacrificial ox trusts the celestial whetstone.
Fortune and misfortune intertwine,
Existence and decay must be self-evident.
Excrescences are but clods of earth,
How can the fox’s eloquence be trusted?
Shen Gong turned back his chariot,
Yuan Gu pressed on to the end.
Chaoxu and Xu You shamed the pure stream,
Shu Shi was called a worthy minister.
I sing the song of gathering lingzhi,
No longer ensnared by cherry or netting.
To leap forward as the lame turtle,
Honor and disgrace—what cause for alarm?
Those who steal names are base as Tian and Shi,
What sorrow in their brewing and acceptance?
The beauty of a man lies in his birds and calves,
The jian bird is not in Cao’s peril.
Confucius returned, lowing like a calf,
Duke Yu departed in wonder.
Xi Fu was no mere reed,
Sai Shu’s *qilin* was in vain.
To sharpen oneself is to summon the distant wind,
Through a thousand ages, all return to the same beauty.

Alas, Wei Zhuangzi,
Why sigh alone?
Gathering feng grass, I walk and sing,
Forever bound for the mountain forest’s retreat.

Heaven and earth are but forms and vessels,
Yin and yang wield their gathering and chaos.
The myriad breaths surge in tangled motion,
Handle and socket—how could they meet by chance?
Dregs and chaff sink in delusion,
The colt’s snatching—what equality is there?
The plain path values steadfast integrity,
Holding the pattern, one sees the center’s design.
Que and Jie relied on plowing’s bounty,
Lian and Huan kept their purity and grace.
Xian Zhang declined the fish-drawn carriage,
Chen Yu severed the sheep’s trail.
The inch-long worm transforms to blue and yellow,
Slander and praise—beware the wooden duke.
The *Wei Feng* laments the *Cypress Boat*,
The river’s flow—how swiftly it passes.
Lin Lei stood silent,
Gathering orchids, he sang in the hidden thicket.

The morning sun rises on the eastern trees,
The faint moon drifts over the western peak.
The Milky Way’s rushing rapids draw near,
The flocking birds join in song.
Spring and summer’s climates differ,
Cold and heat each follow their course.
I long for distant companionship,
This man’s orchid lapel is fragrant.
Far removed from the world’s dust,
Only the faint echo of jade’s music remains.
Why speak of lofty aspirations?
My feelings stir as I hand over my hairpin.

The numinous shade dims the sun’s brilliance,
A pure breeze enters the bed’s curtains.
The swallows nest in their old eaves,
The shore’s geese take flight on high.
The courtyard trees flourish in southern glory,
The river’s flow hastens eastward.
Bramble and thorn choke the road,
Hesitating, where shall I go?
Ascend that lofty mound,
Where mugwort and artemisia spread in profusion.
Go, go—speak no more,
For black dust easily soils the robe.

The distant eastern mountains stretch on,
Winding northwest through orchid groves.
Where do I fasten my girdle’s jade?
The fierce wind blows the evening chill.
Frozen mists congeal in the day’s cold,
Frost and dew make the journey harder.
I grieve for this fragrant essence,
Lest it be marred by weeds and decay.
The spring’s flow sobs in sorrow,
The dark cicada wails in the empty hills.
The hidden lingzhi—vainly I seek to pluck it,
How can I alone find peace?

The eastern mountain stands high and level,
The stream’s current runs deep and swift.
Soaring birds take flight on high,
Floating clouds gather in layered shade.
Spring’s fragrance thrives in a hundred blossoms,
A mournful wind sways the sunlit grove.
Flourishing and withering—like morning and dusk,
In old age, I vainly lament.
Why scheme for wealth and rank?
The empty window shames a thousand gold.
The purple mushrooms of Shangshan bloom,
Yet what heart did Yuan and Qi truly hold?

Driving the chariot from the western city,
The outskirts teem with fragrant trees.
Misty drizzle dampens my timid robes,
Thick shade veils the courtyard gate.
The cold sun sinks into the long river,
The southern road stretches far.
Long have I been parted from my home,
Step by step, I turn to look back.
Within a hundred years of life,
How many times does fear and dread arise?
The bright moon shines on the lofty ridge,
The stars number but four or five.
I gaze in melancholy—where to go?
The autumn wind’s song at dusk.

Winter’s chill arrives,
The north wind blows through the poplar garden.
Falling leaves cry the autumn’s voice,
The evening light shines on the western pavilion.
I know not that the night is not yet spent,
The stars’ radiance gleams and multiplies.
Feeding the horse, I cross the solid ice,
The traveler sighs at the road’s difficulty.
I ponder my lifelong aspirations,
Hard to express in following footsteps.
The ice strings draw forth wondrous notes,
Their lingering echoes drift among the clouds.
I lift my head in thought through the ages,
The flickering candle faces another year’s cold.

In the northeast stands a fine tree,
At dusk, the faint wind chills.

The rains linger on the road for years,
Floating mists still soar and scatter.
The evening sun descends the western ridge,
Its lingering glow illumines the secluded chamber.
White dew overflows the steps,
The Milky Way dips low, then rises high.
I throw on my robe and rise to pace,
Why so much inward sorrow?
I fear only that my aspirations will be thwarted,
Grasping my hair—I see it swiftly turn gray.

**Intending to Roam as an Immortal**
North of the verdant mountains grow the magic mushrooms,
On the lofty ridge stand trees of splendor.
Their fragrant petals gleam morning and evening,
Branches and leaves flourish on their own.
I long to soar with feathered pendants through the heavens,
To transcend the world in lofty reclusion.
I lift my traces beyond the azure stream,
Gaze afar at the oranges by the limpid pool.
Once, Master Fuqiu built his hut,
Forever chanting, he rode the light gale.
With towering vision, he spied the steep isles,
Soaring and wheeling through the circling winds.
Far-reaching, he roamed the six directions,
Scorning the arts of Xu You and Han Kang.
Singing boldly, he followed the luminous tracks,
Serene, he rested in the hidden depths.
Hearing the clamor of the profit-seeking world,
I hide in the mountains, far from the crowd.
Why strive for a carriage and four?
What need to return to my lotus hut?
I climb the forest-clad ridges,
Grasp the marsh grass and gaze over the clear stream.
The layered peaks invite lingering,
How could I again don the long robe of office?
On Mount Kongtong, the hidden pillar-scribe,
In the gardens of Zheng, one leaps in reclusion.
When understanding dawns, the great bird takes flight,
When transcendent power surges, the deep fish soars.
Dwelling unseen beyond mist and clouds,
I chant aloud, gazing toward the primal beginning.
A numinous peak towers ten thousand fathoms high,
Within it dwells a student of immortality.
Mist congeals on the cliffs and valleys,
Clouds veil the springs and dust.
Who can fathom what manner of man he is?
I hear he is Ge Hong.
He lifts his traces toward Luofu,
The elixir of immortality grants long vision.
His chariot and canopy turn northward,
In the forest of pearls, he awaits the phoenix’s tread.
The Jade Maiden has departed—shall I follow?
Cold and light, I spread my wings.
Qu Yuan’s lament finds no path,
Why gaze ahead, awaiting what?

**Intending to Summon the Recluse**
I pace the layered heights, grasping the handle of reclusion,
Treading the secluded path through winding turns.
The forest’s shelter is no mere construction,
Thorns and brambles fill the desolate corner.
Orchids grace the lofty marsh,
Their lingering fragrance veils the encircling home.
Distant peaks stand jagged and steep,
Towering trees rise in solemn majesty.
Here, one relies on plowing and herding,
The fields and acres already store their harvest.
Why then be bound by worldly ties?
The steep valleys are my joy.
In Shangluo, I secretly tend my garden,
On the high mound, I rest with Chang Ju.
Why linger in hesitation?
Truly, I long to sing with Jie Yu.
I recline in the heart of the forest,
As the last rays of the setting sun spread their glory below.
Below lies a winding clear pool,
Enough to wash the dust from my cap-strings.
Amid the deep green and dense growth,
Pines and cassia stand firm and steadfast.
Thickets and thickets of mugwort and wormwood,
Cold springs gleam in solitary clarity.
Few can wear both sash and virtue,
Yet retreat and solitude may be embraced alone.
Carrying my basket, I tread the wild path,
Like Chao Fu and Xu You, free from entanglements.
The perfected one does not climb the former slope,
The great transformation rides this course.
I gaze in melancholy—with whom shall I find accord?
Hesitant, I clasp my lingering fragrance.
My long-held admiration finds no match,
Pacing the courtyard, I stand in vain.
Whom shall I follow in my wandering?
That man sleeps among the reeds.
At dawn, I climb the western ridge,
At dusk, I return to the eastern marsh.
The lofty ridge stands like a towering screen,
Lush trees flourish in dense array.
I yearn for Yue, sighing at the wind in the bamboo,
Longing for Yang, lamenting the dew-laden blossoms.
Why do the trees of the forest stand in vain?
Floating clouds veil the layered peaks.
Empty nests cling to slender branches,
The numinous shade shelters the secluded dwelling.
My clumsiness needs no waiting,
I long only to rest in the vaulted canopy.
Shunning profit, my feet stand firm,
Where shall I raise my sleeves and settle?

**Intending to Present My Form to My Shadow**
All things share a single root,
Fullness and emptiness are their constant.
Heaven and earth are also forms and vessels,
Their flowing movement relies on soft and hard.
Vigorous and yielding ever unceasing,
Why grieve within the Great Harmony?
This floating life is but an illusion,
Yet the numinous light reveals good and ill.
Success and failure are but fleeting shadows,
Aspirations thwarted, hard to align.
Chasing and racing in defilement,
Drowning brings calamity upon oneself.
Let your inner light shine, steadfast and bright,
True virtue knows no bounds.
At dusk, be vigilant in your steps,
Straying brings frost and ice.
I wish to gird myself with these words,
Hoping thereby to strengthen myself.

**Intending My Shadow to Answer My Form**
Our traces are both like morning dew,
Walking this form, we prize likeness.
Heaven and earth are a vast loom,
Yin and yang—how can we fathom their workings?
The ten thousand beings weave in profusion,
Chasing and racing in clamor and glare.
Darkness daily deepens the obscurity,
Sinking and drowning in filth.
Abandoning purity for stench and impurity,
How can we return to the bright illumination?
Ah, the sagely and wise,
Their admonitions are vast and essential.
Treading the furrowed path is like walking on ice,
Reverent care alone brings flourishing.
Be sincere in cultivating yourself,
Lest you fall into the scorn of a hundred years.
The great transformation shares a single return,
In clarity and emptiness, behold the wondrous.

**Intending an Ancient Theme**
To nurture the heart is to see Heaven’s principle,
Movement and stillness cycle without end.
Rightness and destiny are fundamentally one,
The celestial endowment is deeply hidden.
The august words of the sages,
I take to heart with my very lungs and liver.
To fulfill one’s nature is to hold fast,
To preserve it is no arduous task.
The subtle and minute lie in focusing the One,
Abiding in reverence turns back the rushing torrent.
Swift birds must curb desire,
Heat and cold arise from agitation and stillness.
Heaven’s vigor should be unceasing,
The mechanism of transformation moves in cycles.
Sincerity in oneself establishes the ultimate,
Returning to unity is no hard thing.
Alas, those who draw distinctions,
Sighing at the darkness beyond their ken.
They grasp the moon like the historian of Jin,
Or shrink like the cicada of Qin and Zhao.
In silence, I renounce the vain pursuit,
My indignation and pacing deepen my sighs.
How could the great and noble,
From ancient times, harbor such sorrow?
I look up, yearning for the ancients,
To fathom the divine is the grand vision.

**Miscellaneous Poems**
Morning shadows gather the sun’s radiance,
Wind and rain come from the northern grove.
The seasons shift, the creatures change,
The rows of trees deepen their shade.
I recline in the quiet of the courtyard,
The garden birds pour forth their sweet songs.
I look up, cherishing the ancients,
Sitting cross-legged, embracing emptiness.
I admire Yuan Xian’s lofty path,
While Zigong laments poverty’s encroachment.
In the numinous realm, I rest in tranquil illumination,
Hiding my depths, I take up the task myself.
Lofty feelings align with reclusive ideals,
My solitary sighs scatter my serene heart.
Dragging my sandals, I sing of *Shu Li*,
My distant traces remain among rivers and peaks.
The dawn stars gleam with lingering light,
The full sun beautifies the graceful trees.
Until daybreak, the shadows hum softly,
Clear frost weighs on the clustered chrysanthemums.
By the shore, wild geese call in flight,
Reeds on the islet veil their lush green.
The beauty lies beyond the autumn waters,
Her graceful traces beyond the steep valley.
The ways of kings and hegemons fade into antiquity,
Like Yuan An’s noble and fragrant steps.
As the year wanes, I long to follow,
I prepare my carriage, lingering in hesitation.
Winding through the morning sun’s glow,
Suddenly, I am deep in the forest’s curve.
Dawn and dusk bring shifting weather,
The garden and grove scatter their lingering cool.

Falling blossoms drift in the fading light,
As dusk approaches, dragonflies hum low.
Early summer’s heat has not yet burned,
Fragrant grasses intertwine by the pool’s edge.

Weary, I rest beneath the pale moon’s glow,
While frozen gusts brim with white dew.
I linger in admiration of Zhou Xie,
And lie in repose, cherishing Guan Ning’s ways.

Lofty vision grieves the illusory flux,
Yet concealment or display rests in man’s greatness.
My heart delights in the call of springs and stones,
Discarding sandals, I sever all floating entanglements.

In early summer, chilling winds still blow,
Scorching heat has not yet come full circle.
Fragrant trees spread their leaves like clouds,
Morning birds clamor, seeking one another.

Hidden blossoms adorn thickets and groves,
Pathside grasses grow soft and lush.
As the sun sets, I rejoice in finding refuge,
Where thorns and brambles veil the lofty hills.

Life passes swift as a galloping steed,
All attachments are but fleeting shadows.
Feeding taro to delude the troop of monkeys,
I cast off the body—what fault is there?

Pursuing the Dao is like brewing wine in a gourd,
Why should I harbor cares for a hundred generations?
Born with no intent to engage the world,
The ways of the vulgar are not mine to know.

This body, illusory as morning dew,
Yet joy unfolds with each dawn’s light.
Beholding heaven and earth in their vastness,
I see all as a single swirl of gathering and scattering.

Embracing poverty, I sense wealth’s toil,
Holding to lowliness, I forget rank’s peril.
Ban Biao cherished antiquity,
Zhou Dang’s integrity was rare and strange.

Discarding strife, I shed sharp contention,
Fortune and misfortune are not mine to bequeath.
If the world lacks men like Qian Lou,
To whom shall I speak these words?

In bitter winter, motion never ceases,
The four wilds lie beneath layered gloom.
At dusk, floating clouds race,
Sorrowful winds stir the sparse woods.

Perched birds call from familiar branches,
Yearning for spring, I utter a hidden chant.
My carriage, greased, stumbles on past tracks,
My wings, once spread, now seldom sound in flight.

Far off, I entrust myself to the secret summons of the profound,
Roaming freely, I renounce the dusty hairpin.
Light and shadow dart like lightning,
How can I ever align with the bamboo’s steadfast heart?

Gazing afar, I rest upon the sunlit ridge,
A lone soaring bird vanishes beyond the towering peaks.
Beholding the boundless transformations of the myriad things,
Who could suffice to anchor my heart?

Suddenly, the morning air softens,
Clear and bright, unobscured by haze.
My gaze flows beyond the eight horizons,
Nurturing the sprouts of all creation.

Sweet rain murmurs at the eaves,
Spring’s warmth suffuses all with gentle radiance.
Morning winds stir the lofty groves,
The vast river flows on, boundless.

I recline among my books,
Emptying my mind to follow the ancients’ intent.
The dust’s fetters still my swift flight,
Passions’ grime cools its burning heat.

Why seek Pang Meng’s summons,
Or pledge myself to Xue Fang’s pact?
I lament those who chase after trivial ends,
As the vast heavens reveal the Emperor of Images.

---

**Autumn Meditations**

Fierce winds roar through the towering trees,
I stand dismayed, knowing autumn has come.
Morning light transforms valleys and streams,
Day and night, clouds drift across the sky.

Prolonged rains dissolve the scorching season,
Dense shade hastens the cicadas’ urgent cries.
I linger, moved by the passing of time,
Parting my robe, I cling to solitude.

Fleeting lives are like gnats and mosquitoes,
Their breaths and chirps all alike.
I sigh with Yin Xi’s lament,
And long for Hong Yao’s companionship.

Wandering, I entrust myself to the central grove,
Yet where are the steadfast and few?
Greed and strife vie for hooks and bait,
How can one ever be free?

The dark sage wished to remain silent,
Who will understand my sorrow?
Bitter rains swell the cold pools,
The sorrowful terrace wails through the night.

Mournful crickets echo through courtyard and door,
Wild islets lie beneath drifting mist.
Grasses and trees grow ever more sere,
Striking my breast, a thousand cares arise.

The bright lamp stirs the bed and zither,
Yet tuning their notes yields no true sound.
Far distant are the transformations of the Yellow Emperor’s age,
While petty men’s resentments swell within.

Gloom spreads its excesses,
The altar of Kan rises and falls with dawn and dusk.
Through the night, I lie awake, restless,
Vainly nursing regrets and remorse.

Since ancient times, sinking and rising have been our lot,
Exhausted, how can we journey far?
Gazing broadly, all is but a fleeting instant,
For now, I release my lingering emotions.

Glowing clouds gather at dusk,
Autumn’s air grows ever more desolate.
Frost and dew turn increasingly bitter,
Crickets sing through the cold night.

Morning mist veils the vaulted woods,
Soaring birds rest in hidden marshes.
My bearing, once graceful, now frail,
I am moved to sorrow and lament.

The vulgar vie to be caught in nets,
Few follow the ancient ways’ guiding line.
Dark vapors shroud the crossroads,
The restless trample through brambles and thickets.

Song Yu lamented the sorrowful wind,
The divine ruler gazed up to the steadfast model.
I feast on clouded wine and fallen blossoms,
And aspire to surpassing virtue, driving my chariot beyond.

Nine cups steeped with orchid’s fragrance,
The withering groves’ chrysanthemums turn pale.
For now, I follow the path of tranquil ease,
Who can bear the world’s reproach?

The crimson sun purifies its scorching might,
The autumn season shifts to metal’s purity.
Morning groves stir with swift winds,
Courtyard grasses brim with white dew.

Falling leaves drift in the faint sunlight,
Grasshoppers sing near the door.
Waves flow across the level river,
I see mandarin ducks calling by the shore.

In seclusion, I speak of late autumn,
The seasons’ sequence—when will it pause?
A thousand ancient thoughts weigh upon the eaves,
Lofty aspirations stretch far into the distance.

Vainly, I feel the sorrow of Hui Lian,
How could I yearn for An Ren’s admiration?
I turn the reins toward the swan’s high carriage,
And cast my cap into the river’s flow.

Delighting in the joys of hills and gardens,
I gaze up and down, relying on hidden contemplation.
Dismayed by the woodcutter’s fading traces,
I sing a vast song upon the desert road.

Embracing my clumsiness, I find harmony beyond the groves,
Nurturing my spirit, all cares dissolve.
Dense gloom veils the solemn and fierce,
The Han’s floods swell through the lofty morning.

Fine trees contend in the flying wind,
Hidden orchids grow long and fragrant.
Living in solitude, I trust in emptiness and tranquility,
The central valley—how desolate it is!

Guo Tai has already donned his cap and carriage mat,
Fei Yi should keep his wheels far away.
Dust-laden winds blaze with cunning,
Stirring unease in my troubled heart.

Without the refuge of hills and valleys,
How could I escape the clamor?
Resting as the cold and heat dictate,
I compose my flesh to endure the dawn’s chill.

A cold spring suffices to purify itself,
One cleansing, and my spirit soars.
I give free rein to my feelings, singing of the valley’s wind,
And urge my steps toward Fuxi and Shennong’s call.

---

**Matching Rhymes with Su Su’an’s "Occasional Thoughts"**

Form and substance are both illusory,
Yet yang’s strength alone remains steadfast and true.
Heaven and earth embody firmness and compliance,
The supreme principle fills the center, vast and profound.

Long have I wandered mountains and marshes,
As spring deepens, the fragrant grasses grow.
Endlessly, I cherish old friends,
Through a thousand ages, we share this same Dao.

I cast off my traces, leaving the world’s entanglements,
And long in words for the cave-dwelling sage.
Pushing through brambles, I dwell in seclusion,
The Dao is present—who can deny me?

The mountain valley’s joys are boundless,
I lie in repose within the central grove.
Dwelling in silence, I guard the deep abyss,
For a thousand years, only this inch of heart remains.

---

**Matching Rhymes with Su Su’an’s Miscellaneous Poems**

Prolonged rains darken the lingering spring,
Hidden birds sing in the fragrant trees.
Falling blossoms drift on the evening wind,
Cold streams are wholly bound and gone.

The seasons pass like rushing rapids,
Floating entanglements vanish like racing ducks.
In clarity, I behold the myriad transformations,
Form and color ever renew and return.

Stillness and rest foster inner strength,
Holding fast from dawn to dusk.
Following the ancients, I wish to remain silent,
Cutting the sprouts to leave room for growth.

The steadfast trunk endures the winter’s cold,
Pines and cypresses—how could they wither and fade?

Cultivation must be timely, weeds and brambles cleared away.
Gazing through the ages, I await the coming of bright virtue—yet it does not arrive by mere action.
A slender moon emerges from the bound isles,
The Milky Way pales beside scattered stars.
Dewdrops gather on the shrubs,
Withered grass shadows the early chirping crickets.
With empty breast I sit through the long night,
Stroking my lingering emotions in quiet lament.
All things are but dust and decay—
Why trouble over life and death?
Sorrow and fear are but fragments of a great dream,
Years and months pass in vain procession.
Why sigh over this? A hundred years are but a shared drunkenness and waking.
The nature of things holds the supreme principle,
Yet form is bestowed alike on wise and foolish.
Profit and harm twist together,
Drowning in them is no act of wisdom.
The sage comprehends Heaven’s virtue,
Witnessing the flourishing and withering of creation.
Nobility and wealth scorn poverty and lowliness,
Yet the heart’s original purity remains unchanged.
My thatched hut spurns worldly toil,
Nurturing simplicity, I dwell in peace.
Zhuangzi awoke to the boundless,
Leaving illusions to rest in stillness.
Zheng and Lie spoke of celestial omens,
Defiantly apart from the currents of their age.
Their parables startled the world,
Yet few heeded their counsel for governance.
Achievements crumble into dust,
Body and name seek no reward.
King Hui recognized the great gourd—
From that moment, he forgot the passing seasons.
A bright mirror illumines beauty and ugliness,
Its radiance never wavers.
Still water reflects every whisker and brow,
Age and youth are not mere outward guise.
Graceful or sharp, they are called strong and keen,
Yet in skill, they are like butchers of dragons.
Lamenting the scholars of a thousand years,
Only a master craftsman can refine them.

---

**Matching Rhymes with Su Su’an’s “Reflections”**

All things arise from a single root,
Branches and stems should follow their nature.
In infancy, we are endowed with spiritual awareness,
None fail to know what they love.
Our natures descend equally as constant goodness,
Yet brightness and obscurity differ like dawn and dusk.
Early teachings dispel deep veils,
Playful neglect forsakes diligence.
Supreme harmony fills the cosmos,
Rich flavors are not worthy treasures.
Illustrious virtue lies in personal practice,
Excellent plans must be embodied in sincerity.
Holding this, I often sigh at time’s flight,
A river moon veiled by drifting clouds.
An empty courtyard bathed in morning light,
Warmth and joy arise of their own accord.
Sparse bamboo sways on the gentle terrace,
Moss on the path shows few footprints.
In seclusion, I delight in quietude,
Worldly affairs seldom press upon me.
Vulgar customs drift with the current,
Uprooting the source—how can they flourish?
Reckless indulgence daily hardens,
Its thought stirs deep unease.
Excess must yield to a different force,
Congealing the Dao is the highest virtue.
Sacred teachings rely on past tracks,
Inner refinement is my true gain.
Beware! Exhort your initial resolve,
Examine and reflect from dawn to dusk.

---

**Inscription on the Painting of Kongtong’s Stone Chamber**

The divine maiden smelted weary jade,
The ruined elder transformed into sacred stone.
This is the root of Heaven and Earth—
Who carved and opened the chambers of jasper?
Kongtong is renowned among the world’s peaks,
Its wonders foremost in the records of the Yellow Emperor.
Its soaring halls stretch into the vast sky,
Embracing truth, I long for distant traces.
Here the reclusive and silent find their place,
Far removed, they harmonize with the azure void.
Dew-mushrooms extend their years,
Frost-pines sustain their nourishment.
Divine lots and treasured jade script,
Elixirs sought in golden liquors.
In pure radiance, evil finds no foothold,
Through hidden teachings, I glimpse the *Great Change*.
By the Yang River, I dream of rushing rapids,
In the Shao Lodge, I rest with the returning crows.
Were there no immortals within the gourd,
The universe’s breath would cease in an instant.
Clouds enfold the hollow dwelling,
Moonlight spills like golden waves at dusk.
Dark ravines bloom with jasper blossoms,
Torrents swirl in ceaseless eddies.
Grasping the spirit, I wander the boundless,
Vast and free, I roam the isles of the sea.
I bow to Lord Guangcheng,
Who in clarity guards the ultimate mystery.

*Volume Eight of the Jianquan Collection concludes*
*Volume Nine of the Jianquan Collection*

**Five-Character Ancient Poems by Celestial Master Zhang Yuchu of Mount Qi, the Master of Non-Action**

**Inscribed on the Pavilion of Purity and Whiteness**
Geomancy moves the primal transformation,
All existence prepares its steadfast unity.
The supreme principle holds wondrous mechanism,
In clarity and emptiness, its radiance knows no end.
Holding fast to the center, one’s nature is bright and good,
Yet turbid obstructions vie to entangle and exceed.
The noble lord knows the essence of benevolence,
Upholding the root, he values conduct and restraint.
Maps and histories fill the chamber’s corners,
Windows and doors open to the forest’s heart.
Vermilion and whitewash exalt the structure’s brightness,
Fragrant vines and blossoms flourish in lush array.
I join the company of venerable worthies,
Discoursing and delving deep with each unfolding scroll.
Imperial kin and trusted vassals of the realm,
They hold fast to loyalty, aiding peace and tranquility.
Autumn frost deepens the pool’s purity,
The cold moon gleams, the river flows in ease.
Gazing afar, I see the dust-bound multitude,
Their fleeting glory like dusk’s dimming light.
The roc soars beyond the celestial pond,
Its wings unfurled, no turning back.
Caps and sashes display worldly merit,
Yet lofty renown is revered through the ages.
May the ancestral altars stand in enduring splendor,
For a thousand generations, their prosperity secure.

---

**Inscribed on the Studio of Silent Learning**
The Great Change foreshadows the embryo’s glow,
Yin and Yang revolve without beginning.
The empty and numinous, wondrous and unfathomable,
In movement and stillness, the supreme principle is complete.
All things share a single origin,
Yet their divisions rarely show clear bounds.
Human culture emerged with Fuxi’s trigrams,
Sages and worthies set the standard and the path.
The sacred learning takes stillness as its core,
The outer dragon then stirs in hidden awakening.
Heaven and man seldom unite as one,
Principle and desire contend in tangled strife.
Outwardly drowned, one hastens in reckless pursuit,
Inwardly swayed, like an arrow loosed in haste.
The limpid abyss is muddied and submerged,
The warp and weft of the loom grow tangled and loose.
To return is like turning the chariot’s shaft,
Swift as startled flight, then suddenly at ease.
If the heart’s inch is bright and settled,
It gleams like autumn’s frost on the river’s waters.
In Yangzhou, a scion of old,
Warm and steadfast, he follows the ancient way.
Studying profit, he examines the source of transformation,
Delving into the numinous pivot, he fathoms the profound.
His poetry aspires to the craft of Bao and Xie,
His conduct emulates Guan and Min’s footsteps.
Nurturing his virtue in times of harmony,
His merit shines forth in glorious display.
Surveying the vulgar currents of the age,
Their perversity knows no end.
Diligence and seeking must never cease,
Holding reverence to find rest and peace.

---

**Inscribed on the Studio of Self-Examination**
The empty and numinous governs the five senses,
The four limbs are bounded by balanced qi.
The supreme principle resides in the heart’s inch,
Heaven and man thus unite as one.
Flattery and vacillation stir the passions,
Worldly desires spread their mutual veils.
Waywardness gives rise to hidden faults,
Peril and danger arise from within.
Congealed depths are dimmed by drowning,
Scorching fires rage in ceaseless blaze.
The canons and counsels of sages and worthies,
From the Luo and Min streams, open hidden truths.
Returning is not a distant path,
Turning inward, like casting away the trivial.
Conduct rests in holding reverence,
The swift steed is stilled by six reins.
In movement and stillness, timing is key,
Vigilance and caution need no deliberate thought.
By the Xiang River dwells a brilliant scholar,
Long versed in the secrets of Qi and Huang.
In learning, he scorns the mediocre,
A Confucian of old, his lofty aspirations firm.
Through silent cultivation, he attains flourishing success,
Inward reflection, he fears only complacency.
At dusk, he trembles as if treading thin ice,
His radiant virtue then burgeons and thrives.
Diligently refining his nurturing of virtue,
Each day he advances, never resting.
To embody benevolence is to bestow it widely,
How could retribution be far or delayed?
The marvels of stillness and response are unfathomable,
Yet the corrupt vie in madness and rebellion.
I wish to admonish the shallow and base,
That bright teachings may rouse their resolve.

---

**Inscribed on the Studio of Continuing the Aspiration**
Heaven and Earth revolve without cease,
This Dao is contained in the Six Classics.
The noble man continues his forebears’ aspirations,
Expansively observing their fulfillment.
The cosmos nurtures essence and vitality,
The earth draws upon the rivers and mountains’ spirit.
In Yingchuan, a distinguished lineage of letters,
For generations, they have worn the cap and sash.
In the forest of words, they stride with lofty steps,
In the realm of sages, their glorious name resounds.
Literary grace and integrity uphold the family’s teachings,
Through hardship, they rejoice in their worthy heir.
Hidden and withdrawn, he soars on outspread wings,
His refined reputation ascends the royal court.
As a worthy screen, his virtuous conduct shines,
His conferred words encompass wise and kind intent.
Lord Wang raises the inscribed plaque,
His profound virtue is loyal and true.
Through tempering and learning, he relies on clarity,
Immersed and nurtured, his inner depths grow limpid.
Accumulated within, it unfolds in wondrous essence,
His splendid verses bloom like jade and crystal.
Gazing upward, he honors his ancestors’ glory,
His noble writings will transmit his illustrious name.
The worthies of old inscribed their words in metal and stone,
For a thousand years, their sincerity remains bright.

---

**Inscribed on the Painting of Yellow Thatched Hut**
The earth’s embrace founds the high and profound,
All transformations arise from the dark and vast.
The wondrous Dao harbors perfect harmony,
Yin and Yang enfold their boundless expanse.
Famed mountains cradle the central pivot,
Their distant gaze towers above seas and peaks.
A single qi revolves within the compass,
The Three Flowers gestate in the sacred enclosure.
Outwardly, they command the spirits’ service,
Inwardly, they grasp the wind and thunder’s might.
With yellow thatch, the humble hut is thatched,
A lone figure treads the cinnabar ravine.
Long ago, he aided the drought-stricken,
As the river surged with leaping whales.
Jade blossoms hide the cavern’s heights,
His successors rise in surpassing splendor.
His glorious renown enhances the divine land,
His dark robes adorn the stalwart horn.
Gazing again at the painting of Master Hu,
His brushwork embodies purity and simplicity.
In profound silence, no sound is heard,
The soaring terrace joins the vast and empty.

---

**Inscribed on the Painting of Frost Seclusion in the Southern Mountains**
The supreme Dao lies distant amid brambles and barriers,
Relaxation and tension require foresight.
The Jade River inspires distant longing,
Quietly nestled in the forest and pond’s seclusion.
Clouds and woods are drenched in nourishing rain,
Wind and springs resound from the lofty hills.
His dark countenance shines like the patterned leopard,
His hidden traces grace the southern wilds.
In tranquility, he finds the heron’s delight,
The faint and distant Jiang and Han flow on.
At ease here, he relies on fertile abundance,
How could he be lost in schemes and plans?
Yi and Lü were not matched by their age,
Yet their hidden virtue was ultimately sought.
Master Zhuang excelled in avoiding harm,
His flourishing presence observed in secluded cultivation.

---

**On Climbing Woodcutter’s Slope on the Ninth Day, for Self-Amusement**
The morning sun dispels the lingering shade,
At dawn’s first light, I step into the secluded valley.
Hills and gardens offer distant refuge,
The world’s net—how confining it seems!
A thousand peaks rise like jade mountains,
A lone spring gurgles, rinsing chiming jade.
The crossbeam gate leans on the lofty hill,
The empty window faces the rippling bamboo.
The seasons respond to the swift-flowing stream,
A toilsome life is truly like a tethered colt.
The noble man is cautious in action and retreat,
What are gain and loss to honor and disgrace?
Praising cunning courts perilous schemes,
Sincerity and trust shame the crooked hook.
Holding fast to the center, I guard fate and righteousness,
In simple contentment, I find ample sufficiency.
Longing for the recluses of Mounts Ji and Ying,
With gourds cast aside, what more could I desire?
I remove my sandals to caress the towering pine,
Pouring rich wine, I face the clustered chrysanthemums.
Autumn flowers display their evening splendor,
For a while, they please the heart and eye.
I let out a long whistle into the empty vastness,
In enlightened vision, I scorn the vulgar crowd.
Proudly gazing toward the Milky Way’s promise,
How could I have leisure to chase the deer?
Dwelling in emptiness, I find nothing precious,
In yielding compliance, I wander without haste.

---

**On Farming**
Plowing side by side in the southern field,
Our crops and plants grow daily more lush.
Sowing and planting, each in its season,
Some we know well, others are new.
The plains and woods hold rich soil,
The springs and valleys invite exploration of their depths.
Weeding and hoeing already feel laborious,
Spinning and weaving fill the nights and days.

**On Farming (continued)**

The plow and hoe echo the teachings of Zheng and Yi,
The First Farmer is revered as the Zhou sovereign’s heir.
My plain heart rarely mingles with worldly dust,
My secluded path clings to cliffs and peaks.
I shoulder my burden and read my books—
What fault lies in this for the world?
Poverty and lowliness bring their own joy,
As Zhuangzi’s boundless tolerance would allow.
I return late from the market,
Yet rise early when dwelling in the mountains.
Wind and frost turn autumn to winter—
Can prosperity or decline last forever?
Fallen leaves still the cold branches,
The harvest rests on thick straw.
Even sages tilled the soil themselves—
How could this not align with the royal Dao?
Like Pang and Ge, who met in humble times,
Fortune and misfortune are not ours to keep.
I sigh for the ancients in their words,
Reflecting on myself, my hidden cares deepen.
Weary and clumsy, I shame the steadfast Ju,
Like the farmer who loathed the creeping weeds.
I bow in apology to the farmers and gardeners,
Cautioning them to clear the brambles with care.

**On Gathering Firewood**

Long have I yearned for the mountains and marshes’ call,
Here I find joy in simplicity and contentment.
Fortunate to escape the snares of the world,
I wander freely, untroubled by solitude.
Returning, I trace the wild paths,
The forest’s shelter as fine as Dun and Gen.
My humble gate is veiled in green vines,
The square pond cradles clear ripples.
Towering pines rise like blue peaks,
Flying springs cascade into jade pools.
At dusk, I hear the woodcutters’ songs—
Their distant words stir thoughts on life’s true nature.
I rest in integrity, forsaking clumsiness,
For what gain lies in reckless haste?
I ponder the ancients’ forgotten sayings,
Entrusting my livelihood to hoe and basket.
Like fish and birds, I fear the snares,
Not the stench of salted depths.
In nurturing my clumsiness, I know imperfect wholeness,
Holding fullness, I guard against overflow.
Embracing the Dao, I grasp the primal mechanism,
While the lost trust in fate’s scales.
Why lament Yuan Xian’s poverty?
Alone, I fathom the cycles of fortune and hardship.
Gazing up and down, my heart’s resolve wavers,
Time slips by in fleeting moments.
I wash my feet, casting off my tassels,
Singing wildly to cleanse my hidden frustrations.

**Night Sitting in a Mountain Dwelling: Recording My Thoughts**

Secluded and obscure, far from worldly schemes,
In quiet solitude, I find true delight.
At dawn, I summon the carefree to join me,
Their distant steps slow with plain staffs.
We empty the spring wine to the last drop,
The garden’s greens grow in abundance.
Anxious yet glad, they stay the night,
The window hums with wind and spring.
Dew on the grass stirs the evening insects,
Stars in the woods gleam through the open sky.
The fragrant pool reflects the new moon,
Mountain air clings to the fertile earth.
In stillness, I harmonize with ease,
My slow pace content with nurturing.
Like the cicada shedding its filth,
I drift in emptiness, free from ailment.
Long have I strayed from Shang and Hao’s paths,
When may I dream of Zhuangzi’s garden?
The firewood burns through the long night,
For a while, I bid the world’s burdens farewell.

**Returning to My Mountain Dwelling in Late Summer of the Yihai Year: A Spontaneous Verse**

Late summer’s lingering heat blazes,
Yet my secluded hopes align with my plain heart.
Fields and plains are veiled in lush green,
Streams and islets gleam with dark clarity.
The farmhouse rests in quiet, its chickens and dogs at peace,
The overgrown path embraces the deep woods.
The round pool reveals its sacred structure,
Layered peaks unfold in towering array.
Lotus vapors brush the morning dew,
Fish waves ripple beneath the dense shade.
I cast off my cares and find tranquility,
Washing my heart clean in the mountain stream.
Not from pride do I leave the world behind,
But to nurture truth, I must rely on myself.
The autumn wind stirs early longing—
I pour my heart into the zither of the hills.

**Inscription on a Painting of a Secluded Mountain Dwelling**

My plain calling finds its finest in seclusion,
My youthful travels taught me to return early.
I read not for official rank,
But wander the hills with staff in hand.
I chose this wild land to build my home,
Where woods and waters stretch in ease.
A stone bridge spans the empty ravine,
Evening mists nourish the lofty peaks.
Delighting in plowing and fishing,
I decline all offers, content in retreat.
Old friendships have long faded,
My talents seek no external use.
The painting captures this beauty,
Its lofty spirit flowing in quiet streams.
Gazing at my dull and stubborn self,
I leave my form among these hills and vales.
Unrolling the scroll, I awaken to its goodness—
From now on, I await the years’ endurance.

**Evening Thoughts in a Mountain Dwelling**

A lone pine stands in the twilight valley,
Autumn thoughts fill the hills.
Here, among pines and cassia, I find my place,
Weary wings know when to return.
The autumn wind grows sharp and cold,
The pond’s ripples chime like jade rings.
Fallen leaves adorn the sunny ridge,
The thorn gate is draped in meadow orchids.
I rise to open the window, setting my scattered thoughts in order,
Distant chimes fade into the evening air.
Evening dew dampens the clustered chrysanthemums,
I crouch, my joy diminished.
Troubles and blessings, faults and fortunes pass—
In obscurity, there is no blame or hardship.
Virtue shines brightest in harmony,
Turning inward, I find inner peace.
Understanding heaven, I have long grasped fate,
Finding joy where I rest, content in my place.
The great transformation is but a bubble’s pivot,
The cosmos vast as a floating gourd.
Clear frost settles on the thickets,
Time slips by in an instant.
The cicada’s wings do not cling to the clouds—
Why sigh over delayed admiration?
My remaining years I entrust to stillness,
My outer cares lost in hidden depths.

**Winter in a Mountain Dwelling**

I follow my plain calling with steadfast resolve,
My lofty spirit unconfined by the world’s cage.
A trickling stream echoes on the distant path,
I lean on my staff and return to the secluded valley.
Wild sparrows chirp at the daytime door,
The square pond brims with cold green.
Swift winds scatter the clear air,
Frosted leaves glide through the forest’s curves.
I touch my heart, my resolve shaken,
My feelings bound by the world’s net.
Yet my humble gate offers enough for rest—
Why should I envy the crane or the woodpecker’s perch?
Long have I relied on Sun Deng’s wisdom,
Why trouble Ji Zhu with divination?
I entrust my remaining years to nurturing truth,
Who can sway my desires with fate’s decree?
My lineage is bound to heaven’s order,
Yet I grieve for the lost, stumbling in sorrow.
In earnestness, I shame my shortcomings,
In cultivating virtue, I ponder emptiness.
With clear vision, I yield to the flowing stream,
Discarding worldly burdens and needless haste.
What I mourn is my unfulfilled longing,
Its echoes lost in the distant hubbub.
Thick mists veil the distant peaks,
The clear sky gleams with frost and moon.
Cold streams chime like jade pendants,
Dew falls as the stars align.
The high pavilion congeals in mist,
A biting wind cuts through the cold.
Turning inward, I stand firm in fate,
Dwelling in patience, my resolve unwavering.
The yellow bird rests in the hill’s corner,
Its haste and stumbles born of worldly dust.
In vain, the eloquent wander the empty valleys,
Their dark mysteries long cherished.
How could I blindly follow the vulgar chase,
Where gain and loss break the steadfast spirit?
The enlightened find joy in heaven’s will—
What need have they to witness the vast emptiness?
In perfect harmony, the primal oneness is revealed,
Washing away my hidden frustrations.
For now, I delight in the plum and bamboo’s fragrance,
As the year ends beyond the ice and snow.
Basking in the warmth of the southern eaves,
The morning sun warms my humble home.
Dripping dew chimes in the clustered bamboo,
Ice creeps through the forest streams.
The winter plum blooms amid the snow,
The grasses bend with the wind.
The four seasons turn in their cycles,
The new sun dawns in the boundless sky.
Layered peaks are veiled in thin mist,
The murmuring stream soothes my ears.
Reclining in the clouds and waters’ quiet,
In clarity and emptiness, I find my rest.
Who in this world is not bound to fate?
To fulfill one’s nature lies within oneself.
I lament past faults, yet embrace obscurity,
Chastening my beginnings to walk with care.
How could I fathom the workings of the primal mechanism?
I follow the ancient path, looking to those who came before.
Raising my head, I sigh to the azure heavens—
To whom could I speak of gathering herbs?
My dull and stubborn nature,
I leave behind in these hills and vales.

**A Small Drink in the Mountains, Presented to the Two Recluses Wang and Ji**

The first sun warms the dawn after rain,
In quiet delight, we meet by chance.
The humble cottage basks in morning light,
Forest and stream abound in clarity and space.

By chance we prolong the joy of clouds and waters,
Who would call this gourd-dwelling narrow?
Long have I cast off the dusty world’s passions,
Birds and fish now greet me with ease.

Emptiness and tranquility move with the Dao,
Detachment only deepens heaven’s freedom.
I see clearly how phoenix and roc pursue their paths,
While others drown in the dusty net of day and night.

I sigh in admiration for Zheng and Li’s summons—
How could I be swept away by drifting waves?
Ashamed of my dull and waning faculties,
I retreat in stillness to the brambles and wilds.

What fortune to join such venerable elders,
Our bold songs stirring the crisp autumn air.

---

**Spring Rain**

Fine rain gathers on the lofty hills,
I turn homeward to the white-clouded peaks.
Entangled in worldly cares, my thoughts drift,
Yet in the heart of the forest, I find contentment.

Water and trees lend their quiet ease,
The fragrance of spring deepens my intent.
Leaping fish dance in round bubbles,
Joyful birds sing in the shaded groves.

Near the ravine, the stream begins to swell,
Falling blossoms encroach on the overgrown path.
Ashamed I lack foresight,
My heart remains empty, my thoughts serene.

Heaven’s Dao moves in silence,
Sincerity alone resides in the plain heart.
Vigilant cultivation brooks no delay—
Who else shall bear this resolve?

---

**Water Pavilion, Dispelling Care**

A chance meeting lifts distant aspirations,
In seclusion, no worldly ties entangle.
The square pond opens to quiet chambers,
Water and trees hold lingering clarity.

Endless rains weary the wandering floods,
The hollow silence harmonizes with my nature.
The garden’s depths offer a mirror for stillness,
Within, brightness aligns with purity.

The wind-swept ravine suddenly roars with cascades,
Lofty peaks fade into hidden depths.
Young bamboo sheds its first sheath,
Wildflowers scatter their last petals.

Fields and valleys deepen in summer green,
As time passes, worldly cares accumulate.
The dark and undivided hold to fate’s decree,
I briefly share the gulls’ and egrets’ pact.

---

**Night Lodging in the Eastern Garden of Yousheng Abbey, Hangzhou**

In youth, my ambitions spanned seas and mountains,
Before manhood, I studied poetry and books.
Deeply I admired the traces of mountain recluses,
At peace with the world’s contrary ways.

Once I wandered freely in Qiantang,
Now I rest in this garden cottage.
Old friends once shared close ties,
New acquaintances bring cautious joy.

I recline in the shade of green paulownia,
Singing aloud the Yellow Oriole’s song.
Bamboo by the window parts the first rain,
Moonlight spills across the front steps.

Oranges swell with frost’s roundness,
Reeds stretch across the vast lake.
Friends gather like cranes in a flock,
My idle heart aligns with lofty principles.

At the first word of parting,
My heart and steps grow distant.
The sunbird cries in the mournful wind,
Cold tides descend on the withered plain.

Five years pass in fleeting moments,
Reflecting, I linger in hesitation.
Seated, I feel the weight of time’s decay—
Why cling to the immortals’ constraints?

At dawn, I rouse my distant longing,
Resolved to return to my fields and garden.
The sound of Wang Qiao’s reed pipes and cranes
Soars alone into the void.

---

**Basking in the Sun**

I love the sun’s gentle warmth,
Thin clouds slowly disperse.
The barren mountains gather cold shadows,
Courtyard trees stand sparse and withered.

The lowlands still lie submerged,
Yet the fields offer humble refuge.
Millet and wheat fill the furrows,
But the harvest leaves many granaries bare.

What can I do to set things right?
The world’s ways diverge from my path.
How could I know the joy of warmth,
Still reaching the scattered and the frail?

Heavy frost withers the hundred grasses,
Hidden blossoms mingle along the garden path.
What offering could I make to you?
Only to clear the overgrowth within.

The vast spirit of high antiquity lingers,
Its depths suffice for endless contemplation.
I cast myself into the quiet shore,
Content with this life’s measure.

Surrounded by walls overgrown with brambles,
Cool shade covers the garden’s green.
I endure the wind and rain’s assault,
Never clashing with the world’s currents.

Few visitors disturb my carriage’s wheels,
Few thoughts bind my heart.
I eat simple fare, seeking no excess,
Wearing worn clothes, sitting in meditation.

Yet old habits breed dust and obstruction,
Illusions steep me in their warmth.
If I do not cherish what lies before me,
Fleeting distractions will chase one another.

Who has plumbed the harmony of heaven and earth?
Mind and world await restoration.
Great indeed is the trigram *Gen*’s beginning and end,
Its noble fruit joining the mountain’s trees.

---

**Gazing Over the Wilds**

The north wind whips the raging waves,
The river runs turbid, unclarified.
Oxen and dogs traverse the level ridge,
Trees shed their leaves, mountains lie exposed.

Light mist scatters across forest isles,
A solitary bell tolls from the perilous city.
Moored, I cannot sleep,
The long river murmurs through the night.

My worn clothes weary of travel,
The lingering rain brings the cold.
Worldly moods shift between dawn and dusk,
This fleeting form—what shall it meet?

The reeds and mallows whisper mournfully,
I can only sigh and clutch my breast.
When the sky clears and the wind stills,
Morning clouds drift past the distant geese.

River grasses glimmer in faint sunlight,
Reed isles scatter wandering tracks.
Turning homeward, my heart eases,
Weary, I rest among the mugwort and thistles.

My form dwells within this bounded world,
This floating life follows nature’s end.
Success or failure—why dwell on them?
A hundred sorrows only vex the heart.

Hold to sincerity, return to nature,
Cultivate yourself in timely balance.
When shall I cast off my clumsiness,
Forever trusting in the wind of Chao and Xu?

---

**Lodging at Qingyuan Abbey, Former Residence of the Immortal Ge**

The Dao’s pattern moves in subtle ways,
The perfected one hides his sacred traces.
This lofty structure stands in a famed town,
Once I wandered here, moved to the depths.

Far from the dust of winding lanes,
A winding path circles the crumbling pond.
Pond grasses thrive in evening dew,
The light pavilion echoes with tall pines.

The hall’s hempen curtains frame the vaulted image,
Its splendor faded, I sigh for the remnants.
Mysterious threads follow the steps of practice,
The well’s turtle and the western beam endure.

A separate chamber invites a shared drink,
Lamps flicker as the room stirs.
Through the night, my thoughts grow still,
Looking up, I lament the lost legacy.

At dawn, I set out to explore,
Cautioning myself to diligent cultivation.
The divine work is not remote—
Through the ages, it illumines the dark.

---

**Mountain Journey on the Second Day of the Third Month, Jiaxu**

Rain clears from the front peaks,
I urge my staff along the homeward path.
Overgrown trails wind through spring grasses,
Wild waters cross the level bridge.

Joyful birds sing in round, clear tones,
Plowing oxen tread with measured steps.
Abundant springs murmur in shaded ravines,
Dense bamboo gleams in the inner garden.

The sacred peak opens to an airy pavilion,
Thorn gates guard the cloud-bound fastness.
New streams overflow the pond,
Lush greenery fills the windows.

I sweep the terrace, arrange the scattered books,
Leaning on my staff, I gaze through the brambles.
Hills and groves suit my delight,
How could I vainly admire the world’s filth?

In emptiness and detachment, I praise distant traces,
Yet perilous affairs caution my hidden tasks.
How could I sever worldly ties?
Only among trees and stones can I find deep refuge.

Weary wings rest in the branch’s nest,
The lost may yet awaken to my understanding.
For now, I indulge my reclusive heart,
Life’s meaning lies in the farmer’s plot.

---

**Ascending the Former Site of Lord Wen’an’s Xiangshan Shrine**

Fu Xi and Yao embodied heaven’s movement,
The kingly Dao upheld the web of human relations.
Shun and Yu inherited the sacred vessel,
Their single-mindedness shone in transmission.

**Ascending the Former Site of Lord Wen’an’s Xiangshan Shrine (continued)**

When Zhou fell, the *Ya* and *Song* odes faded,
Confucius spoke in alarm.
Yi Yin aided the mandate’s reception,
While Mencius upheld its propagation.
Great was this profound canon’s mystery,
Its radiance shining through a hundred generations.
Yet through decline and renewal it passed,
Brightness and obscurity defying heaven’s constancy.

The Lu-Wang school revived the hidden lineage,
*Jianzhong* continued the ways of Yu and Tang.
Like uncut jade from Qingtian and Jingshan,
Its vast renown gleamed pure and bright.
The heart’s inch governs the numinous and subtle,
Obscurity brings no harm to truth.
Movement and stillness embrace the perfect principle,
Ever vigilant, one strengthens within.

Sacred teachings blaze like sun and stars,
Noble conduct outshines ice and frost.
Here, scriptures dwell in a land of grandeur,
Ancient traces deepen the primal resonance.
Snowy halls gather by lamplight at night,
Spring rains linger in the wind-swept courtyard.
From Guan to Min, the branches spread,
While Wu and Chu are graced by its lingering fragrance.

My dull nature shames my ignorance,
Yet I am fortunate to follow these teachings in detail.
I ascend cloud-capped peaks to pay distant homage,
Where Buddhist shrines lie hidden in brambles and weeds.
I seek out Lu’s former abode,
Where overgrown fields rise to lofty ridges.
With reverence, I gaze in awe,
As the autumn sky clears under the sun.

Emerald terraces embrace the foreground,
Vast and distant, all returns to the finest trace.
Fleeting observations spur me to follow the ancients’ steps,
Daring not to glimpse the boundless wilds.
Rapids rush past—who can stand as a pillar?
The great tone—who can serve as its phoenix?
The eight directions turn like wheels,
A thousand years look up to this radiance.

---

**First Day of the New Year, Guihai Year**

The first sun alters the year’s course,
Long rains at dawn begin to scatter.
A gentle warmth heralds spring’s nurture,
Clouds and things thinly unfold.
Clear streams disperse along secluded banks,
Fine birds call through carved thickets.
Plum blossoms drift along mossy paths,
Clusters of bamboo crisscross sparsely.

Pond duckweed gathers tender green,
Dense algae hold pure ripples.
Delighting in these principles brings contentment,
For nature’s essence surely holds abundance.
Another year shames my aging teeth,
My dull learning—what end shall it find?
As dusk approaches, I guard solitude,
The girdle’s words are well worth inscribing.

---

**After the Lantern Festival, Rejoicing in Clear Skies, Ascending Jing Tong Hermitage**

Spring’s warmth suffuses gentle harmony,
My frailty eases, my breath finds rest.
The hermitage stands in solemn emptiness,
My secluded quest now spans years.
A narrow path is lost beneath fallen leaves,
Vines and creepers whisper through the void.
Plum blossoms scatter lightly,
Bamboo and pine intertwine in splendor.

Stillness ever clears the spirit,
Sunlit peaks line the window like dark brows.
Lantern-lit nights mingle with market clamor,
A lone crane soars beyond the sky’s bounds.
I press my hand to my heart, filled with reverence,
My simple trust clings to profound reliance.
Weary, I lean on the grove’s shade to return,
Here I grasp the suspended solution.

---

**Inscribed on the Dream Crane Pavilion**

The perfected one attains the hidden meeting,
His steps and breath transcend form and sleep.
Things transform like dreamt encounters,
The embryo immortal shares a numinous bond.
In the spirit’s realm, he chants in a stone chamber,
The worthy one hones his will through study.
Moonlight over the pool rises through vine shadows,
Peaks and forests adorn the courtyard in emerald.

His eastern writings embrace profound awakening,
The myriad beings illumined by balanced *qi*.
Leaning on his desk, he hums the *Gao*’s melody,
Serene and joyful, free from the slightest care.
Graceful as the wind’s passage,
Swift as a unicorn’s flight.
I look back to the pavilion’s past elegance,
Butterflies and ants now scorn the dust’s neglect.

What use is baldness to release from bondage?
Riding in a carriage—empty as Duke Wei’s honor.
Sorrow and misfortune stir emotions,
Life and death—who can cast them aside like Zhuangzi?
Entangled in turmoil, all perishes,
Concentrated in emptiness, floating visions are clarified.
I shame my longing for cap and sash,
Yet spread my wings, urging my wheels to soar.

In vast harmony with the mountain’s disciples,
A thousand years stretch into distant flight.

---

**Viewing the Dug Spring**

The hermit tends his plow and spade,
Delighting as the spring’s source flows freely.
Drawing water from afar brings no fear of toil,
Finding the spring, he shares it with neighbors.
Servants grow weary yet rejoice,
The world calls it a divine work.
Tracing the source, the stream grows clearer,
Stones gleam, the ravine runs full.

The perfect transformation nurtures the primal sea,
Its ceaseless flow vast and boundless.
The ten thousand differences share a single principle,
Tracing back reveals beginning and end.
Gathering the gaze, not even a ladle’s worth,
Yet who can fathom its day-and-night labor?
I lament those dull and ignorant,
Who fail to glimpse the root’s origin.

From this, I embrace seclusion’s purity,
Drinking and rinsing in the wind of Chao and Xu.

---

**Cold Rain**

Night rain gathers lingering cold,
Morning bells enter the wooded hills.
Withered branches cry in the fierce wind,
Spring torrents run clear enough to rinse.
Woodcutters return to smoke-wreathed doors,
Mountain birds rest on frosted citrons.
My breast holds hidden sorrow,
My thoughts are calm, free from strife.

Fields and wilds grow daily barren,
Heaven’s harmony fears injury.
My solitary heart—with whom to discuss?
My halting steps shame the worthy successors.
Gazing at the scene, I feel the ebbing tide,
Separation—who can bridge it?
Cultivating the heart lies in constancy,
Brushing my sleeves, I cast off worldly dust.

---

**Inscribed on the Hall of Continuing Goodness**

When the jade tablets emerged after Qin’s fall,
How many teachings nearly vanished?
The perfect principle lay buried in brambles,
The imperial heart—how could it stray?

The Lu-Wang school revived the fading thread,
From this, heaven’s benevolence was seen.
Integrity and goodness are innate norms,
Practice and study make them ever more true.
Clarity and subtlety share a single root,
The profound should be worn at the girdle.
Surveying antiquity, I follow the sages’ counsel,
Beginning and end—all is bright and pure.

The young scholar inherits his family’s learning,
His goodness upholds plain sincerity.
Mountain radiance glows with spring’s moisture,
Lush forests hold the evening’s mist.
Discourse and song harmonize with friends’ benefit,
Admonitions are well worth heeding.
From this, I steel my resolve,
The ancients’ tracks are worth pursuing.

---

**Inscribed on the Cold Wind Terrace Painting**

Master Zhuang awoke to the myriad’s breath,
Who can discuss *da sheng*?
Looking up and down through the cosmos,
Decline and flourishing are as fleeting as a hair’s weight.

This man admired steadfast conduct,
Resting here by woods and streams.
Bright moon crosses clear torrents,
His empty song enters the drifting clouds.
Flying geese are too distant to glance at,
His lingering melody cherishes spring’s warmth.

---

**Inscribed on the Pure Capital Hermitage of the Spotless Chen Dongtang**

Embracing truth, he awakens to serenity,
Delighting in this dwelling among woods and valleys.
The elephant’s foothills offer refined seclusion,
All encounters are old and familiar.
Peaks gather around his desk,
Stone ravines twist and turn.
Autumn rains resound in rushing torrents,
Spring clouds moisten plow and hoe.

A winding bridge steps over mossy paths,
A remote isle connects to woodcutters and fishermen.
Lush trees offer evening repose,
Hills and gardens suffice for his joy.
I know he has long left the dust behind,
His inner cultivation fittingly hidden in emptiness.
His forebears’ virtue matched his distant aspirations,
Their radiance ever accompanies him.

Yesterday, I visited his gate,
Morning winds scattered yellow leaves.
I bowed deeply, washing away distant longing,
Our parting at dusk was deeply hesitant.
His pure teachings find few in the world to match,
Yet I have long held them in my breast, no fool.
The model belongs to the venerable,
Who can follow its unfolding and rolling?

My past longings have grown vast and distant,
My secluded traces surely hold abundance.
His advanced years stand firm as a pine,
His dark bond is rich and true.
I wish to receive the Pure Capital’s teachings,
To be shown the jade casket’s scriptures.

---

**Eastern Garden, Composed for Wang Jingzhou of Qiantang**

The immortal transcendents lodge in hidden realms,
Shedding their traces to lightly float beyond the floating world.
The great recluses are not bound by worldly dust,
Forgetting form, they may dwell in secluded retreats.
Such a man possesses refined purity of bearing,
Unfettering the mind to open the bound pavilion.
His fragrant garden vies in secluded construction,
The jade palace shuns gaudy splendor.
Around his four walls flourish lush plants,
The empty courtyard spreads its first feast.
Bamboo grows thick with verdant feeling,
Curtains and screens hang in emerald shade.
Within the yellow chamber, ritual classics reside,
Before the purple tower, dream clouds gather.
Riding cranes, he traverses the notes of the sheng,
Rinsing at the well, he communes with cold springs.
The eastern dawn has long faded,
Yet dark virtue should be esteemed and advanced.
Long ago, I wandered west in vast travels,
Where the numinous halls harmonized my circling steps.
Lofty paulownia shaded the sparse windows,
The crackling firewood heard the red strings’ music.
Evening horns scattered the morning rain,
Autumn tides followed the moon’s fullness.
Lakes and mountains slowed my leisurely steps,
How could worldly dust entangle me from without?
The venerable elders lent their aid and support,
With empty heart I wandered the Great Mystery.
Do not delay in answering the Gate of Envy’s call,
With penetrating vision, perceive all things before they arise.

---

**Departing Jingkou at Dawn**

Through mist I set forth, the oars creak loudest,
Parting the river where perilous waves thin.
The cold city wears a sash of misty willows,
Autumn waters embrace the wind-tossed reeds.
Light rain dampens the forest’s southernwood,
Congealed frost veils the islets’ withered grass.
My tiny boat meets the wild islet,
I push open the secluded door to unfold old maps.
The quiet chamber reaches its utmost seclusion,
White clouds linger beneath the eaves.
Transcending worldly dust, I forsake high reclusion,
Like Master Zizhen, I should dwell in valley retreat.
His posthumous writings fill the old tent,
His talent and feeling move the bound heavens.
Fine verses reveal his splendid literary grace,
His travels inquire of ancient ruins.
Slanting mists suddenly form crystalline patterns,
As swift oars urge hastening words.
Pushing back the awning, I capture fleeting inspiration,
Exhorting myself to embrace tranquil emptiness.
Distant blue mountains mark his path,
The ebbing tide hints at presence and absence.

---

**Ascending the True Man’s Chamber on Mount Fanghu**

The sacred peaks bear auspicious omens,
Where immortals wander in jade palaces.
His lofty aspirations are called outstanding,
In the divine capital, he pays homage to the flying dragon.
Discoursing with scholars of the Jade Hall,
His broad vision traces the tracks of golden steeds.
Brush and ink double in value,
Yet he still recalls his forest wanderings.
The golden immortal bears the sea’s grace,
The dragon well nests on lofty peaks.
Secret teachings suffice for casting the linchpin,
Concentrating spirit, he guards the ring’s center.
Through rugged paths he traverses valleys and ravines,
Early forsaking the dust’s obscuring haze.
In Min and Yue, autumn’s sighs resound,
Clouds veil the forms of Yan and Tai.
Returning east, he revives faded elegance,
In learning, we often follow one another.
Brush and paper pour forth like sunrise,
Painting and calligraphy pursue vast perfection.
His seal script reveals Han dynasty traces,
Clerical script humbles Qin’s seals.
My modest nature is dull and inferior,
Grasping the inkstone through spring and winter.
By the stove and crucible, he sits amid plum snow,
By the tides and oysters, he chants to the creek’s wind.
Admiring orchids, he pours out the sea’s depths,
His wise discourse shines in Jiangdong.
In youth, he roughly possessed virtue,
In the capital, he toiled in attendance.
Famous regions rely on his esteem,
How could noble rank and lofty status be prized?
Returning with pendants, his hair already yellow,
Suddenly withering amid the secluded cassia groves.
Sorrowful longing cuts deep in reverence,
The jade forest stands desolate and empty.
Ten years have passed in distant departure,
Soaring high like the crane from Liaodong.
Morning frost transforms the suburban scene,
Libations and offerings hasten to thorn and thatch.
Our literary bond shares sighs of lament,
Our spiritual natures hope for hidden communion.

---

**Rhapsody on Leisure**

Ceasing worldly ties, I lighten the dust’s harness,
Dispersing cares, I embrace tranquil emptiness.
Mountain rains deepen summer’s green,
Forest mists rise from twilight peaks.
The creek’s clamor presses near the courtyard,
Emerald grass fills the deep pond.
Tall trees daily grow lush,
Young bamboo also casts cool shade.
Each thing’s nature finds its own fitting place,
Flourishing and fading share a single heart.
Soaring high, I admire distant paths,
Chasing shadows is but vain pursuit.
The inscribed teachings illuminate past sages,
In solitude, I vigilantly guard against sinking.
Subtle feelings I entrust to poems and scrolls,
Few gather to discuss, why not lift the hairpin?
The wondrous principle is possessed by all,
The numinous source flows deep in hidden seeking.
How could I follow false traces,
Obstinately lingering in the empty forest?

---

**Morning Thoughts**

Emerging at dawn, frozen thoughts already stir,
A gentle wind fills the tall forest.
The fading river glimmers toward dawn,
Sparse stars fade in the wutong’s shade.
Village lanes wind beside distant islets,
Cocks crow, scattering the clustered woods.
Morning mist veils the fragrant trees,
Night’s haze lingers on lofty peaks.
Pine torrents cascade through the valleys,
Walking alone, I traverse rugged paths.
Falling branches are wet with scattered dew,
A desolate coolness fills the empty space.
Delighting in dwelling in secluded beauty,
Long weary of the dust’s cage.
Strolling the wilds, I indulge in leisure,
How could I be enslaved by mixed pursuits?
Rivers and springs fatten the carefree form,
Clouds and trees nourish the woodcutter’s heart.
Far removed, I forsake worldly entanglements,
Soaring high, I distance myself from ornate hairpins.
Flowing springs echo the unhurried staff,
Striking my zither in the hills.

---

**Ascending Mount Huagai**

The imperial carriage establishes the primal destiny,
The numinous traces reveal the divine foundation.
Surpassing the great peak of Mount Hua,
His celestial truth long held the hidden handle.
Fortunate to follow and trace these steps,
This visit fulfills the earlier promise.
Profound secrets open the dark teachings,
Abundant merits adorn the deep rites.
Refining form, he achieves the golden elixir,
Laying down his halberd, he ascends the cinnabar radiance.
Kongtong’s cliffs open a cliffside altar,
The empty altar spreads a chessboard.
Thunder rumbles in the hollow caves,
Spring veins contain cold moisture.
Transforming scenes display mighty marvels,
Jade banners gleam in linked flight.
Distant traces adorn successive generations,
Rivers and mountains vie in secluded wonder.
In late years, he receives his long-held admiration,
Climbing and studying, he hastens to pursue.
The clustered mountains vie in hairpin adornment,
The side paths wind in perilous coils.
Flying cliffs startle the spirit’s eyelashes,
Revolving peaks race like jade dragons.
Clouds stretch like bright silk,
Waters curve like delicate threads.
Valley echoes carry the bamboo’s sighs,
Forest fragrance scatters like coiling rainbows.
Jade palaces record their construction,
Illusory blessings renew thatched huts.
Guest lodges open to secluded views,
Eaves protect the cold mist.
The eight directions reach their limits,
Myriad differences gather in subtle traces.
The world’s realm looks down upon the dust’s altar,
How lofty and low are Song and Hua!
Weary, I rest amid mist and haze,
Gazing afar at the vast celestial steps.
Supreme virtue shines in pure prayer,
The immortal’s plan fulfills hidden hopes.
The vast expanse merges in primal unity,
Who can fathom its beginnings and ends?

---

**Visiting the Jade Prosperity Palace on West Mountain**

Beyond the world, I deeply admire the distant,
The high immortals’ numinous traces.
The mighty capital stands by Jiang and Han,
The dark halls array the layered peaks.
The sun’s essence nurtures the heavens’ seasons,
Heaven’s order shines on Jin’s eastern bounds.
Strange dragons wreak people’s calamities,
A foot-long sword achieves divine merit.
Dark construction commands wondrous beauty,
The supreme spirit is revered in succession.
I, unworthy, am a true heir,
Tracing these steps is my proper path.
Cascading ravines pour forth singing rapids,
Fertile fields are veiled by sparse pines.
Wandering pines seem like village cottages,
Winding paths echo with forest bells.
Weighing cypresses stand in remaining lushness,
Dried springs flow with pure, faint murmurs.

**Moss and Ruin**

Desolate moss surveys the old structures,
Ancient sites thrive with dense, hidden thickets.
The tower’s wheels lodge in vast emptiness—
Where now is the radiance of cinnabar splendor?
The common folk are bathed in gracious blessings,
Daoist disciples hold fast to profound devotion.
Rivers and hills ever revolve in motion,
Their governance reflects the august heavens.
Night’s qi sobers the forest’s silence,
Spring’s harmony scatters the gentle breeze.

I secretly trace Jing Dan’s wondrous path,
Shedding the mundane—how could I follow later?
I steel myself, gazing up at the tracks of the ancients,
The grand vista stretches boundless and endless.

---

**Inscribed at Chengzhai**

The square and round revolve through the six voids,
Stillness and movement ceaselessly interact.
Motion and rest root in the primal origin,
Subtle congealment pervades the Three Realms.
How vast is the heart of the worthy and sage!
Embodying sincerity, it abides in no fixed place.
Their profound teachings roused Zou and Meng,
Exhorting the self through inner vigilance.
Vigilant cultivation yields Confucian exemplars—
Yan’s dwelling upheld reverent caution.
Cultivation and nurture enhance clarity,
Subtle mysteries emerge through remaining strength.
Behold the workings of the primordial transformation:
The myriad beings mutually sustain and plant.
Within, this is the great root made firm;
Flourishing and decay are but dust and pebbles.
If the wandering vapors are purified and clear,
Dark creation gleams like metal and stone.
I aspire to master the art of return,
Vigorous practice aligns with the *Great Change*.

---

**Orchid’s Ascent**

The secluded orchid thrives in lofty bowls,
Delighting in the warmth of the morning sun.
That sprout unfurls its fresh beauty,
Hidden, it flourishes with fragrant verdure.
Upright in emptiness, its steadfast stem stands,
Luminous hues diffuse its pure fragrance.
Its nature finds affinity with the plain and true—
How could it exist for mere auspicious favor?
Yet here it rises in the forest’s depths,
Remote and silent, unknown to the world.
Fine trees mingle with dense thickets,
Renowned blossoms root in numinous soil.
Their grace surpasses all other flowers,
Their purity harmonizes with noble kin.
Vigorous growth in its prime,
It draws sustenance to nurture rare fragrance.
Gentle breezes brim with dewy splendor,
Dense mists condense in subtle perfume.
Rich rains moisten its lush abundance,
Radiant light illumines the clustered greenery.

Its refined conduct aspires to the sages’ model,
The *Li Sao* mourns Qu Yuan’s lament.
Wandering freely, I long to pluck and wear it,
Yet distant travels are but dust and vapor.
The empty chamber befits steadfast solitude,
Fellow wanderers grow ever more distant.
Auspicious signs await early covenants—
What need for haste between dawn and dusk?
The eight directions gather in vast vision,
The dark mechanism returns to the source of transformation.

---

**Returning to Xian Spring in Winter**

At dawn I tread, ashamed of my slow progress,
Returning to rest amid the beauty of grove and valley.
The outskirts’ creatures harmonize with the seasons,
Wild paths embrace the winding stream.
I speak of turning toward the white-clouded peaks,
Mist-laden trees retain their lingering green.
Shallow rapids guide the cold current,
Lofty ridges don the mantle of fine woods.
Barren fields have yielded their harvest,
Secluded dwellings nestle in forest huts.
Long have I cherished tranquil serenity,
My wise words align with simple desires.
A light wind washes the dust from my robe,
A gentle rain nourishes my anointing.
Weary, I rest—worldly ills fade,
Perilous snares avoid even paper’s touch.
Ever have I hoped for Xian’s summons,
My refined conduct accords with steadfast solitude.
Worldly taints surely entangle,
Yet the hidden true self ever suffices.
Shaking my garments, I ponder deeply,
Striving in silence to rely on pine and chrysanthemum.

---

**Evening Banquet at Immortal Rock on the Twenty-Third of the Sixth Month**

Last night’s rain dispelled autumn’s gloom,
I sought the hidden, drifting on clear islets.
At dawn I prepared for the secluded tryst,
True delight befits the waning heat.
Flowers and petals display linked fragrance,
Elders and worthies excel in worldly discourse.
Gentle currents cradle shallow sands,
Distant rapids secretly connect to the shore.
Sheer rocks scatter like the loom’s supports,
The limpid pool swirls with cobalt depths.
Duckweed and gulls dot the snowy blossoms,
Sandpipers float like silver threads.
Wild vines darken the dense shade,
Distant mountains girdle the light rain.
I explore wonders to the farthest seclusion,
Only then do I find the path to Cloud Rock.
The numinous cavern coils with tiger and dragon,
Divine traces open the hall’s doors.
Deep moss obscures kitchen and granary,
Verdant creepers drape the loom’s frame.
A mighty whistle severs all dust and haze,
An empty song stirs the mist and fog.
A single chamber hangs from the cliff,
Seats arrayed on level sands for debate.
This gathering transcends the common—
Harmony and awe mingle with cups and platters.
Had I not attuned to the immortal’s tune,
Years would pass like Penglai’s isles.
Sincerely I visit the ancient shrine,
Ashamed my steps lag behind the dust.

Red Mound commands the wild and strange—
Fitting that wind and thunder guard it.
Through boundless kalpas, I view fleeting bubbles,
A single impulse washes away a thousand ages.

---

**Composed While Watching the Rain**

Early summer suffers from ceaseless rain,
Towering trees luxuriate in lush growth.
The stream roars with sudden surging torrents,
The peaks stand pure, residual haze bright.
Lush greenery shades the eaves and pillars,
Tall bamboos lend their cool to the secluded.
Heavy burdens of human affairs grow rare,
Mud and mire halt the wheels’ progress.
For now, I find solace in letters and ink,
Holding to the Dao lies in nurturing and following.
Hidden virtue embraces the abyss within,
From the subtle it reaches the vast and deep.
Dare I hope for recognition like the Mo and Si?
I can only sigh in admiration of the lofty mountain.
Yin accumulates, succeeding the scorching heat,
I shame myself for worldly thoughts.
Sitting, my mind wanders to the sun’s song,
Vast and boundless as the source’s spring.

---

**Inscribed at Jingzhai**

Enduring principles possess constant nature,
Sacred teachings restore the primal origin.
Pure essence, inherently good and keen,
The Confucian school treasures its jade-like brilliance.
The *Odes* and *Documents* tread the ancients’ path,
Through a hundred generations, they bloom anew.
Holding reverence lies in unity,
Solemn and respectful, I roam the vast dwelling.
