Lakes and mountains stand in solemn splendor,
Leisurely joys match the river’s perch.
In office during a clear reign,
I partook in the *Canon* and *Counsels*.
Gentle and profound, I harmonized with dark simplicity,
My refined bearing illuminated the realm.
Abundant cultivation hopes for lush growth,
Inheritance and succession await the heir’s gaze.

---

**Occasional Verse on a Late Outing**

The bright pond brims with fragrant islets,
New currents swell in joyful surges.
Dark clouds drift past the rustling trees,
The sheer ravine scatters the cold mist.
Human tracks grow sparse in mud and mire,
Twilight deepens with birds and frogs.
Distant thoughts stir memories of past trysts,
Clustered cares weigh on pressing duties.
Resting in seclusion, I attain this ease,
Yet worldly concerns still entwine and coil.
Vain traces chase the dust’s birth,
The true source wondrously abides nowhere.
Spring’s splendor swiftly yields to another year,
Frailty and age deepen my shame and longing.
Gain and loss follow the workings of transformation,
Hills and gardens suffice for measured steps.

---

**Mountain Rain**

Early heat returns to the old dwelling,
The vermilion sun’s fire grows ever fiercer.
Lying ill beneath the central grove,
I recline in stillness, free of care.
The windy ravine roars with rushing streams,
Field frogs croak amid dense thickets.
Fish glide lightly through fragrant algae,
Mist settles over the towering forest’s shade.
Verdant feelings rise in tall bamboos,
The empty courtyard thrives with intertwined branches.
Gathering clouds suddenly form a downpour,
All night the torrents rush in.
The lotus storm crosses the morning’s chill,
I cast aside my hairpin to tend the brambles.
Smoke and waves stretch far, free of dust,
Heart and trace remain serene, lofty, and aloof.
How could I compare to the mosquito’s drone?
Why trouble myself with birds’ play?
Vainly I sigh—my long-held aspirations thwarted,
Confinement deepens my distant yearning.
Anxieties and indignation remain unresolved,
For now, I find solace in the flowing stream.
I speak of following the recluses’ path,
Forever parting from the human world.

---

**Composed While Walking the Southern Ravine**

Grateful for my humble thatched hut, I return to my staff and ascend for a distant gaze.
Hills and forests brim with autumn’s qi, ravines and valleys gather blossoming grasses.
Shaded gullies veil faint clouds, layered peaks stand stark and solitary.
The plain, drenched by passing rain, lets fallen leaves dance lightly in the wind.

Alas, I am trapped by ill fate, my retreat not for show but true withdrawal.
Bedridden, my strength wanes daily, the cost of medicine shames me—no small sum.
I know regret and shame grow ever longer, gain and loss invite only scorn and ridicule.
Choosing what to grasp, I see only filth and loftiness; rushing to flatter, I mimic frowns and smiles.
I scorn the careless who chase the current, sighing at those who clamor for rank in vain.
Silken threads may yet serve some use, but a cracked jar can never ring clear.
I rest my body, tending my jar, content to meet the lotus’s shade.
Why mimic those who weep at life’s end? I rejoice in the whistling of Su Men’s heights.

Heaven’s decree binds my inmost heart, in silent stillness I guard the subtle workings of the Dao.
Pity the narrow-minded, who day and night consume themselves in flames.
All transformations must find their return—casting aside my hairpin, I take up fishing rod and line.
Handle and socket fit not where they’re forced; steadfast integrity need not gleam.
Flattery swiftly turns to wolves, mercy and pardon depend on the light of wisdom.

After the snow, early spring returns.
The recluse cherishes pure wandering, steadfast in solitary virtue.
Winter’s long mildness brings joy; returning, I tend to firewood and herds.
The clamor of dust is washed away at once, the vast and empty long content me.
Snow and frost veil layered clouds, wind-swept cliffs stand with lone trees.
The first plum holds all fragrance, dried pools seep with cold green.
Opening the window, I arrange old scrolls; lighting kindling, I trim the bright candle.

I grieve at the world’s snares entangling me, weary, I shed its bonds.
Forcing myself through treacherous paths, I find overgrown trails where pines and chrysanthemums wither.
Fortunate to receive the gaze of enlightened favor, I lay bare my past regrets.
Who among later scholars will take up the hairpin and saw? I only long for the company of deer and friends.
This age’s miasma drives me to haste, its twisted wheels crush my heels.
My heart scorns the carriage’s path—how could high or low be mere fence and touch?
I wish to join the silent and secluded, washing my ears by the winding stream.
Not lacking the butcher’s whetstone, I shame myself for chasing sheep in flattery.
My mat warmed by Gou Lou’s pines, my oar awaits Shan Yin’s bamboo.
I entrust myself to the year’s cold season, ice and frost nurturing withered fragrance.

As dark yin yields to spring, how swiftly time flows!
Awakening to illusion’s fleeting nature, I see emptiness holds no desire.
How base are those who chase perch and trout, who rush for carp and rot!
A thousand years pass in idle words—raising my voice, I return to the deep valley.

**Early Autumn Rain at a Mountain Dwelling**
Summer’s rain melts into autumn’s chill, faint clouds dampen the lonely wheel rut.
Seeking the source, I visit my old hut; climbing the ridge, I find homes far away.
Rice lies low beneath the crossbeam gate, a sacred spring gushes from hidden peaks.
Quiet summits gleam with jade-green hue, fallen leaves spread across lofty ridges.
Morning calls mingle with fine birds, my steps leave no mark on silent moss.
New streams wind around the courtyard, plants grow lush with verdant feeling day by day.

Embracing this love for the central grove, how could I be bound by worldly dust?
Though my body is broken, I trust in great years; clumsy, I follow the crooked path.
Not lacking the company of Sun Deng, I still hold Ge Hong’s encouragement in mind.
Having seen the world, I bid farewell to drifting duckweed; how could my wild passions be shallow and clear?
I celebrate Master Li of Le An Hall on his eightieth year.

**For Master Li of Le An Hall on His Eightieth Birthday**
Through countless kalpas, long life endures; like mountains, the tortoise and crane endure.
The celestial court belongs to the virtuous elder, great years rightly bestowed early.
Awakened to illusion, he has long savored harmony; in his jade chamber, he sips the essence of blossoms.
Nourished by the plain words of Confucianism, he preserves and nurtures his sincerity.
Joy resides in the humble gate’s gatherings, in winter’s cold, his hall stands deep and sturdy.
Morning winds bring timely rain, evening waters still in autumn’s dusk.

His will is firm in refined bonds, delighting in the alliance of cap and coarse cloth.
Cloud-waves wash his jasper mat, moon-dew fills golden stems.
At peace with simplicity, he adorns himself like a turtledove; gracefully, he follows the steady path of the rushes.
Outlasting the sun’s glow, his name stands as a model for sacred peaks.
The dark reckoning lingers in slow years, his hidden truth guards the host of spirits.
Thus his white hair endures forever, his penetrating gaze transcends the divine classics.

**Wandering the Immortal Crag**
The sacred peak crowns Penglai’s realm, autumn’s clarity brings crisp and cool qi.
I drive my words beyond the world’s bounds, casting my oar to roam the profound and secluded.
Streams and islets embrace winding paths, shoals and rapids rise in meandering ascent.
The River Lord’s palace emerges from water, heaven’s loom weaves brocade as a screen.
The immortal altar stands on Han’s foundation, tiger roars echo through empty space.
Gazing in reverence, I step into the jasper palace, where cinnabar cliffs array wondrous forms.

Celebratory brew fills my gourd, Meng Ji’s silk still spins on the loom.
Seeking and exploring, my interest wanes and waxes; my unbound spirit surpasses past longings.
The great vessel towers like a flying tower, refined gold blazes in the vaulted image.
Evening libations end solemn discourse, each talent pursues their own measure.
At dawn, we depart from the limpid pool’s edge, gentle ripples ripple in vast expanse.

The immortal’s traces venture into peril and strangeness—what sorrow could surpass this itch?
Jiang’s quilt stirs deep feeling, Chen’s glue envies flowing talent.
Wang Gong’s appearance grows ever purer, Wu Meng’s will must be vast.
Words sharp as Yuan Hong’s, discourse as rich as Guo Xiang’s.
Islands and islets lie hidden like Peach Blossom Spring, riverbanks and hamlets flourish in view.

Who asks the way to this world’s end? Illusory words—why deceive with floating lies?
Sparrows and quails chase dust like equals, the literary unicorn shames worldly thoughts.
Earth’s expanse stretches beyond Qi and Bo, heaven’s music knows no bounds between sky and soil.
Content, why cling like monkeys? Trusting, gulls come and go freely.
I prepare to sip chrysanthemum blossoms, gazing afar—who yields to the past?
Browsing lightly, I record what I’ve seen; my distant thoughts fix on the empty and vast.

Glory and decay swiftly shift through ancient and modern—let refined bearing test bold abandon.
If not of gold and stone, one must miss the dark pearl’s net.
Raising my head, I await the immortal’s return—how could I forget the lofty wind?

**Setting Out at Dawn on the Divine River**
At dawn, I set out on the sacred stream, my distant intent drawn to the river’s trees.
Wild huts cling to village dwellings, morning mist scatters over cold islets.
Wheels pound distant rapids, bathing birds drift on deep shores.
Frost and dew linger in thickets, layered peaks rise like phoenixes folding their wings.

Returning home brings its own comfort, parting stirs thoughts of kin and old friends.
Long estranged from worldly hopes, our bond shines bright as the morning star.
My haste was never long—how swiftly the seasons turn to dusk!
Drinking from my gourd, I feel little ease; loosening my robe, I rest in scattered dew.

**Moonlit Night After Snow Clears**
Northern snow clears at dawn’s glow, peaks stand like heaps of blue jade.
Lingering in the empty forest’s gaze, my free spirit soars through heart and eye.
A wild boat drifts on the fading current, desolate mist thins over sparse huts.
Layered branches flourish with elegant form, thickets hold the last of winter’s green.

Holding rare aspirations for this vast world, I refine my heart to few worldly desires.
My secluded dwelling delights in reclusion’s virtue, my many scrolls rely on past exhortations.

My distant traces stir far-reaching thoughts, yet my lone flight need not falter.
To hold inner brilliance is to value steadfastness; to delight in antiquity is to find contentment within.
The myriad transformations share the same qi-mechanism—yang unfolds, gentle yet deeply stored.
No shame in the inch-long toad’s stretch, for I harbor a pearl within its casket.
The full moon purifies the frost’s glow, lofty sentiments rest among the courtyard bamboo.

**Secluded Dwelling, Self-Content**
The sky clears in spring’s radiance, my secluded dwelling delights in emptiness and spaciousness.
Words follow the handle of mountain valleys, my intent finds joy in forest and stream.
Wind-swept steps dampen with pine mist, the pond’s flow swells with lingering rain.
Rich fires burn fine timber, winding paths keep dust and toil at bay.
Purple ravines guard the dragon’s abyss, blue peaks charm the phoenix’s flight.
When might I meet the reclusive white-haired immortal? My thoughts drift toward Song and Qiao.
Across the eight directions, spirit traces converge; through a thousand springs, I tread in distant reverence.
Virtue’s pursuit is not for long years—observing the countenance suffices for nurturing life.
Thus I rely on straw cloak and bamboo hat, idle and free, refusing the cage’s constraint.
At times I ask of the fisherman’s words, or join the woodcutter’s song in harmony.
The ten thousand apertures each sound well—here I entrust my lingering echo.

**Inscribed on *Summer Mountains After Rain***
Evening rain passes frozen trees, drifting clouds exhale layered peaks.
A bridge stretches through green vines, a staff planted firm at its center.
The mat of cares is washed away, thoughts soar beyond worldly traces.
Is Zhongshan truly beyond reach? The clear rapids sing with lofty melody.

**Inscribed on the *Hall of Subtle Flavor***
Supreme harmony lies in pure simplicity, true flavor values quiet depth.
Fu Xi and King Wen sketched the Great Beginning; Confucius discoursed on emptiness and profundity.
The Way is not distant—walking in integrity, one regards night and dawn alike.
The recluse of the tranquil forest sheds worldly entanglements.
Beyond the clouds, the lofty thatched peak gathers stone blossoms and lingzhi.
Pine roars fill the eaves with snow, orchid sashes stir the wind at the railing.
Within, the spirit’s dwelling stands complete; external distractions fade with the wine’s overflow.
I brew and discard the wine of excess, refining my judgment to subtle discernment.
With white hair, I merge into the One—vast and still, like the potter’s mold.

**Inscribed on *The Living Root Scroll***
Zhuang Zhou awakened to the equality of things, the myriad beings like the wind’s ten thousand breaths.
All plants share a single root—yet strange words grow ever more grand.
Hui Shi’s clumsy use of the great was boundless, without shore or bank.
Not clinging to the window’s scattered form, how could *Zhi Li* ever be fully reckoned?
There was a remarkable man of Huaiyang, long a master in officialdom.
Disdaining the low currents of the world, he soared high, breaking the roc’s wings.
To value clumsiness is to preserve the nest whole; to entrust one’s feelings is to harmonize with night and dawn.
His steps followed Li and Lian, his radiance rivaled Ye and Zheng.
Yet I, drawn to the pebble’s community, find the scattered tree fit only for irrigation.
Across a thousand years, our fates may align—dust’s pursuit brings no sorrow.
The sacrificial ox becomes a tree’s disaster, its fat and lacquer mourned in vain.
I wish to follow the wanderers of truth, a single breath soaring through the boundless.
If our affinities are meant to be discussed, we shall ride the wind swiftly through the heavens.

**End of *Jianquan Collection*, Scroll Nine**
**Beginning of *Jianquan Collection*, Scroll Ten**

**Five-Character Regulated Verse by Celestial Master Zhang Yu Chu of Non-Action Mountain**

**New Year’s Day**
The year begins with signs of harvest’s grace,
Dawn’s light stirs the turning of the season’s pace.
Morning eaves cascade like waterfalls in flight,
Cold trees shroud the brook in misty, muted light.
Human affairs drift like duckweed, rootless, frail,
Life’s course half in water, half in cloud’s soft veil.
Fullness and void follow fate’s unchanging decree—
Why then prize the weight of worldly lore and plea?

**Rejoicing in Fair Weather**
Summer’s advent brings the sky at last to clear,
Leisure’s fleeting ease now gently draws me near.
Deep in woods, the rain bestows its lingering dew,
Low streams reveal the few who wander through.
Evening sun leans on the slanting bamboo’s line,
Garden blooms drift close to books I recline.
Years have made me slow, my ways now dull and plain—
Yet solitude befits this quiet retreat’s domain.

**Sitting in Meditation at the Dharma-Viewing Stele Pavilion**
A rustic pavilion nestled in the wild’s embrace,
Moss-grown paths lament the frost’s untimely trace.
The floating world’s affections thin as paper’s sheen,
Yet in these empty hills, the Dao’s savor runs deep, serene.
Carved cliffs stand stark in crimson, stark and bare,
Trees’ dense shade obscures the sun’s descending glare.
Bending to read the worn stele’s fading line,
My spirit drifts—all sense of self in mist does twine.

**Blue Community**
At dawn I urge my staff through mist-wreathed strands,
Sacred crags lead on to Crane Terrace’s lands.
Spring currents lose their way ‘mid isles untamed,
Day’s rain makes moss-grown bridges slick, unnamed.
Forest huts fade in the haze’s gentle sway,
Fishermen’s straw cloaks linger far away.
Seated, I watch Peng Isle at twilight’s hue—
A single boat washes worldly dust anew.

**Night Sitting at Xian Spring**
Borrowing clouds to cloak my clumsy guise,
Divine peaks affirm this pure realm’s wise.
One stream links twin ravines in silent flow,
A thousand peaks play hide-and-seek in show.
The Daoist mountain awaits its humble scribe,
The numinous dell harbors its hidden tribe.
From this, my anchor in leisure’s embrace,
The floating dust’s reality I question’s trace.

**Returning to Xian Spring in Late Spring**
Late spring seeks the ravine’s secluded glen,
A flowering staff crosses the wild bridge’s span.
Mountain crags curve like jade, dark and deep,
Forests lend their dampness to emerald coils’ sweep.
Willows probe the banks where orioles alight,
Boats rest still on waves where egrets take flight.
This fleeting life I lodge here for a while—
What heights may joy ascend? I muse the while.

**Winter Night in the Hermitage**
Spring stirs before the year’s last days are done,
I lie abed in my mountain home alone.
Cold bamboo bars the path to garden’s gate,
Plum blossoms cast their glow on books I contemplate.
The spring’s voice scorns the barking dog’s harsh cry,
Its ripples startle fish that leap on high.
All things bear the pulse of life’s unceasing play—
In emptiness, I find my joy’s full sway.

**Inscribing "Autumn Colors of the Jade Grove"**
A celestial terrace rises, wrought with grace,
Jade trees encircle the vault of azure space.
Autumn’s hues half-veiled by rain’s soft screen,
Pine winds gust along the threefold garden’s green.
Clouds’ moods retreat to the reclusive hall,
The ravine’s tones mingle with tung and wutong’s call.
I strive to follow those who’ve led before,
Unfurling hidden schemes on Hua and Song’s high shore.

**Inscribing "Secluded Autumn Mountains of Square Gourd"**
The northern park holds boundless, subtle art,
Autumn mountains fill the gaze from near and far.
A humble bridge connects the post road’s thread,
An aged hut stands ‘mid frost-kissed maples’ red.
Evening’s chill seeps in after passing rain,
Scattered clouds dissolve in the hush of sky’s domain.
By chance, this place becomes my hermitage’s seat—
Few traces of the world’s dust here do meet.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (I)**
I love mountain dwelling’s quiet, unconfined,
No wants suffice to nurture truth refined.
Autumn’s voice arrives in the seventh, eighth moon,
Mountain hues shared by two or three alone.
Though my steps grow faint, my heart knows no dim shade,
Though my body’s poor, the Dao is never laid.
Gazing at the vast transformations’ play,
I scratch my head, ashamed of red dust’s sway.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (II)**
I love mountain dwelling’s stark simplicity,
Years stretch long in quiet austerity.
In stillness, I perceive the Dao’s vast span,
In leisure, sense the rush of life’s swift plan.
Summer rains make clouds whiter still,
Autumn winds turn chrysanthemums to gold’s chill.
How fine to sit with feet drawn in,
Worldly cares no longer cling or pin.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (III)**
I love mountain dwelling—here I know at last
That things and self are one, their fates entwined and vast.
Wind and clouds are but the ruts of passing wheels,
Heaven and earth a single ring that seals.
Life’s transformations turn without cease,
Round and square hold mysteries without release.
Inhaling, exhaling—all is bound,
Yielding, I follow east or west unbound.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (IV)**
I love mountain dwelling, where engagements fade,
Stillness and clamor like an anthill’s trade.
Gatherings and teachings—spider’s artifice,
Emotions breed the self, the other’s vice.
Action and concealment show what’s right or wrong,
Who heeds the words of Meng’s old song?
Only this heart, so faint, so fine,
Perceives the truth in silence’s design.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (V)**
I love mountain dwelling—creeping vines repair
My brushwood gate with nature’s quiet care.
The peaks themselves assume their roles as guest and host,
Distant rapids hum like zither’s ghost.
Dogs grow still as village twilight falls,
Mountain depths bring rain that misty veils install.
When night deepens and all motion ceases,
Jade-like tones alone in chanting increases.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (VI)**
I love mountain dwelling—years pass in still repose,
Wind and frost reveal the stalwart pine’s repose.
Ice and snow confront the cold plum’s steadfast grace,
Nurturing the fire, the Three Palaces’ debate I chase.
A hundred cares dissolve in spirit’s ease,
Yet without the cicada’s molt, no freedom sees.
Cast wide, unbound—this is true release.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (VII)**
I love mountain dwelling—here I gather in
The heart that wandered through ten thousand ages’ din.
Drifting delights in the rushing torrent’s might,
Stilled, I see the gold’s pure, unalloyed light.
The world sees only change as constant state,
Human feelings gauge but shallow and deep’s weight.
Kongtong holds no other savor’s claim—
I vow to age within these woods’ domain.

**I Love Mountain Dwelling (VIII)**
I love mountain dwelling—cold and warmth I heed no more,
Rivers and lakes hold no dreams of yore.
Few new friends, the old now few,
I follow my lot, let the world misconstrue.
Words fill my scrolls with parables wide,
Yet when shall this end? I cannot decide.

**Inscribing Wang Yuan’s Eight Poems**

**Spring Clouds over Eastern Gorge**
Stone ravines shaped by clouds’ own hand,
A realm of minor immortals grand.
Cold creeps into the grassy pool’s dream,
Night rain startles the sleeper’s scheme.
Village turns past the neighbor’s tree,
Blossoms drift where the weir’s waters flee.
Seeking immortality, not pride’s display,
I’ve lingered here year upon year’s sway.

**Stone Terrace on Northern Ridge**
Seeking truth in mountain and marsh’s keep,
I turn scriptures into a stone terrace steep.
Evening mist rises from ancient trees,
Spring crows alight on plum blossoms’ freeze.
Feathered pendants glide through clouds’ embrace,
Divine oars return from the sea’s vast space.
Looking down on the boundless shore,
Where is the land untouched by dust’s lore?

**Lush Scenery of Southern Hill**
Southern mounds stand fair, their beauty bright,
Indigo and blue fill the seat’s sight.
One should drink like swordsmen bold,
Or carry books and hoe the field of old.
Autumn’s chill brings yellow leaves in store,
Deep streams ask where white fish roam and soar.
How fine to keep half an acre’s claim,
To share its quiet, hidden frame.

**Autumn Moon over Western Stream**
Moonlight chills the night’s first freeze,
Streams flow clear on either side with ease.
Stars hang slant by the eaves’ low edge,
Wind and dew mingle with the spring’s pledge.
A lone boat drifts past sandy shoals,
Autumn hills conceal the ancient walls.
Fishermen’s songs bring wild tunes near,
Winding paths twist, then disappear.

**Pines and Chrysanthemums by the Thatched Hall**
A grass-thatched hut beside the farmer’s plot,
Surrounded by plants I’ve nurtured and wrought.
No wine to toast a departing official’s cheer,
Yet songs of thatched roofs bring solace here.
After snow, I wander late, chanting low,
In autumn’s depth, I eat what nature bestows.
Long have I probed the furnace and elixir’s art—
How near is retreat? I question my heart.

**Mulberry and Hemp of the Old Garden**
Planting plots with mushrooms and herbs rare,
Hoeing through the years with patient care.
Mulberry and hemp bear life’s intent,
Village groves share their shade’s extent.
Rain swells the woods and ponds’ embrace,
Spring’s chill lingers in the fields’ deep space.
Evening talks hold no idle word,
In old age, true hearts are heard.

**Clear Springs of a Distant Well**
Wells apart hold springs so pure and bright,
Their cool, clear flow meets at the source’s light.

**Luminous Candle as Mirror**
The candle’s glow shines bright as glass,
A rootless stone its base does pass.
The tea cauldron pours ever-green,
The cinnabar ladle draws warmth unseen.
Not like the vastness of Qi’s sea,
But left for grandsons’ longevity.

**Jade Well’s Clear Spring**
Stone hewn to shape a new pool’s grace,
Ten acres green in squared embrace.
Rain’s voice stirs waves where carp once played,
Mountain mist trails dragon’s scent delayed.
Curved treasures chime like falling snow,
Flowing pearls dusk’s stars aglow.
From this I know true flavor’s art—
Early awakened to the *Great Mystery’s* heart.

**Matching Rhymes with Alchemist Xie of Pure Refinement**
Du’s Bend brims with poetic thought,
Secluded dwelling outstrips thatched cot.
In hidden truth, the Five Primes glimpsed,
In nurtured simplicity, the Three Spirits kissed.
Feathered robes traverse woods and vales,
Immortal grace softens doors and halls.
Elders fade, their loss profound,
Yet I rejoice in stars unbound.

**Southern Yang’s Heirlooms**
Southern Yang’s rich legacy,
Ink pools trace its ancestry.
Born where phoenixes alight,
Cranes return to Parrot’s Isle’s sight.
Distant peaks in mist arise,
Towering trees float clouded skies.
Evening stirs thoughts of Wei’s stream,
Fishing hooks cast not—my dream.

**Withdrawing Traces**
Withdrawal’s habit deeply bred,
Observing emptiness, all senses shed.
Pools darken as springs seep through,
Paths shun moss, its patterns grew.
Stone ravines roar with vernal rain,
Purple gates veil twilight’s stain.
I crave the woodcutter’s, herdsman’s cheer,
And bid the world’s dust disappear.

**Five-Word Regulated Verse: Wandering Bi-Lu Grotto-Heaven**
Bi-Lu, true abode of heaven’s might,
A fine morn for wandering’s delight.
Nine days prior, our refined date,
Autumn’s third month seals our fate.
Immortal blooms in clusters rise,
Noble pins join kindred ties.
Streams divide where boats are cast,
Forests and isles pass thick and fast.
Villages near, cups linger long,
Mountain kitchens hum evening’s song.
Steep cliffs hang iron’s weight,
Dense trees ring jade’s chime straight.
Mist weaves Xiang’s curtains fine,
Stars descend on coffered design.
Springs split frost-white mortar’s hold,
Terraces cradle dew-laden gold.
Moonlit feasts with leopards near,
Kitchen smoke with monkeys cheer.
Dawn’s meal hastens sleeves to bind,
Wild flutes end the counters’ chime.
Tree-borne sun gleams ice’s sheen,
Cloud-slumber wraps silk’s sheen.
Perilous paths—cast Xie’s clogs,
Sideways steps—abandon boats.
Grotto gates press shoulders tight,
Cliff paths seek in shared pursuit.
Clambering, we hear jade bamboo’s call,
Pointing, we sit enthralled.
Shady ravines wind wind-worn stairs,
Sunlit ridges wash day’s airs.
Qi’s terrace fits a fallen cap,
Dense mist begs a fur-lined wrap.
Han’s traces hide a spirit-tiger’s lair,
Qin’s seals guard rainbows beyond care.
Lu’s lord deploys armored might,
Tai Yi’s secrets probe the night.
Sacred peaks bear spirit’s writ,
Jade texts grace feathered writ.
Linked fish traverse the strange,
Crows in order, few deranged.
Lush hues revive Su’s tangerines,
Cool drafts pour from Jade Maid’s wines.
Ancient grooves recall Bo’s quest,
Valleys watch for hermits’ rest.
Branches steady, roosting magpies start,
My light step shames the soaring gull.
Perilous ways—only peaks to scale,
Vain words echo, loud and frail.
First tracks follow fragrant tread,
True pacts revere the grand design.
Tortoise steps trace guiding holes,
Chime-bent bows near hooks align.
I, unworthy, bear divine descent,
My talents stray from brush’s intent.
The imperial court praises stillness’ grace,
The mystic gardens grant wandering’s space.
Returning staff startles perched cranes,
Whole life dawns—ox unbound remains.
Illusory names mark cliffs untrod,
Vast kalpas view lofty peaks as clods.

**Matching Wu Yanzhi’s "Wandering Xian Spring"**
Fields and gardens make fine retreat,
Immortal veins trace ancestral seat.
Wei’s Bend now shifts its manors’ ground,
Pan’s divination finds abode profound.
Golden waves part the moonlit mere,
Jade breath pours from lotus’ sphere.
Seclusion suits heaven’s decree,
Cultivation’s work—nature’s artistry.

I delight in valleys’ deep retreat,
Yet gaze upon the capital’s might.
True reclusion follows Pang’s lead,
Seeking depths where Kong once freed.
Lotus remnants part dew’s thread,
Winding streams bear springs ahead.
Stone drips echo hollow jade,
Thorn gates lack embankments’ aid.
Footsteps startle hidden leopards’ rest,
Splendor stirs sleeping dragons’ crest.
Scripture halls stand white and still,
Book forests hush crimson’s spill.
Gathering marvels with friends in tow,
Parting grieves—old ties aglow.
Cranes’ calls suit wandering guests,
Crane-like steps shame lofty guests.
I dare not follow Crane-Crown’s way,
Nor match Deer-Skin’s ancient sway.
Kin and nephews share reeds’ trust,
Tea and nuts our duty just.
Returning, I doubt bamboo’s sight,
Yet talks bond like pine’s embrace tight.
Literary bonds glue tight as lacquer,
Verse rings true as bells’ pure clatter.
Future journeys know joy’s flight,
Front seats await favor’s height.
Glorious deeds outshine forebears’ light,
Household plans—no easy plight.

**Fifteenth Day of the Fifth Month: Wandering Immortal’s Crag**
Immortal traces meet true beings’ throng,
Delighted to share this wondrous song.
This culture reveres the world’s esteem,
A flourishing age looks to sages’ dream.
Talents embrace Hua’s river’s grace,
Journeys span Weak Waters’ space.
Boats drift from market’s bustling shore,
Sipping tea beneath fishermen’s door.
Stone rapids churn like sunlit snow,
Stream waves dance with evening’s blow.
Egret’s light treads secluded isles,
Crane’s stillness graces empty piles.
Grotto gates barely hold the boat,
River cliffs trap oars afloat.
Green cliffs part Yu’s ancient trace,
Blue trees guard Qin’s sealed embrace.
Silk weaves heaven’s craft divine,
Indigo floats earth’s axis’ spine.
Void follows scaffold’s chisel’s art,
Creation’s potter—who imparts?
Yu’s beams stand bold and stark,
Eaves’ lattices meet in the dark.
Birds’ nests startle with sudden cries,
Ape’s dens hide in misted skies.
River Lords hide in deep abodes,
Feng Yi lurks in secret codes.
Lofty winds—where Guo once stood,
Refined bearing—Wang’s solitude.
Ant-wine fills verse’s tally,
Brushes rise to carve cliffs’ rally.
Han’s shrine pines stand ancient, grand,
Luminous pendants grace water and land.
Evening greens draw bells’ chime near,
Fading reds sweep seats clear.
Cinnabar’s glow flashes distant light,
Sword’s aura arcs like rainbow’s flight.
Tigers and leopards lurk in shadowed glens,
Dragons trust the mighty torrents’ dens.
Jade bamboo probes summer’s grove,
Jasper grass cradles spring’s soft love.
Linked jades gleam beyond mist’s veil,
Hanging pearls bathe in moon’s pale.
Mountain brews shame sweetest wine,
Deep pools recall Cloud Dream’s design.
Moss invades the guest bed’s tread,
Pavilions trust torrents’ spread.
Heaven and earth spin vast and wide,
Years and months surge like a tide.
Chanting blends with forest’s sigh,
Secluded vows trust cassia’s high.
Xie’s path shuns peril’s allure,
Zhuang’s words rouse the blind and poor.
Crouching at feasts, I fear grace’s weight,
Admonitions stir my soul’s state.
Words pour like surging seas,
Dao’s lineage looks to Heng’s peaks.
King’s virtue praises worthy’s might,
Ministers embody loyalty’s light.
Green City guards ancestral streams,
Bi-Lu holds divine craft’s dreams.

The Milky Way clears the silent void,
Dust and haze wash through vast expanse.
Nine essentials await carving and grind,
Three benefits stir the dull and deaf.
Parting’s sorrow cuts deeper still,
Discourse on texts exalts meaning’s height.
Renown follows Jia and Ma’s trail,
Pure inquiries trace Penglai’s isle.
Ancient luster gleams with jade’s glow,
A thousand autumns mark the vault’s design.

Universal deliverance ferments joy’s fruition,
Lu’s transmission of immortal office shared.
Sacred peaks store true models,
Mysterious codes awaken filial piety.
Elders return to the imperial court,
Hidden rites convene the immortal pact.
River torches blaze with candlelight,
Cloud-borne feasts convey heartfelt intent.
Expounding rites, the altar stands in awe,
Exemplars refine the canon’s precision.

Verdant slips reach the Crimson Bureau,
Jasper chapters ascend to Jade Capital.
Feathered ministries link Du and Lu,
Households transmit the brimming mystery.
Dragon swords flash with radiant sway,
Phoenix banners gleam in celestial light.
Five-zhu coins dazzle in exchange,
Eight directions hum with harmonious song.
Chariots and guards encircle a thousand officers,
Far-reaching pursuits summon the Six Dings.
Kan and Li refine through purging,
Return and scorn restore the womb’s embrace.
Purple gates congeal in empty vastness,
Yellow chariots gleam with inlaid crossbars.

Rain extinguishes Cold Food’s flame,
Flowers gather in late spring’s clarity.
Three thousand rites soar in swift delight,
Five hundred million names fill jade-bound tomes.
Flying ports advance transformation’s nurture,
Myriad beings sense flourishing glory.
Flame pavilions float pearl-like millet,
Dark seals array the city of fire.
Incense and mugwort illumine dreams,
Black offerings prepare grand assemblies.
Moved by compassion for the poor and distressed,
Startled cries alarm the bound and lowly.
Fearsome voices fill markets and fields,
Auspicious vapors foretell budding ferns.

Springs and soil open layered pavilions,
The ice-wheel moon pierces the Nine Pures.
Yin and Yang revolve in subtle wonder,
Heaven and Earth rely on shaping’s might.
The Dao employs spirit as its function,
Years forget favor—what cause for alarm?
The teaching’s pivot leans on elders’ esteem,
Leadership reveres the model’s weight.
Ashamed to tarnish the duckweed’s stain,
Grateful to receive blessings’ grace.

Henceforth dwell in peace’s realm,
Former glories spread their resounding praise.

**Congratulating Yan Heng’s New Residence**

The state’s foundation stands in grandeur,
The immortal capital’s structure soars.
Peaks encircle the fertile earth,
Springs converge toward the lofty vault.
Rivers and mountains store numinous realms,
Divine brilliance marks the illustrious clan.
Endowed with stern resolve and conduct,
Admiring learning’s virtuous craft.

Sacred grace flows from a mighty source,
Mysterious models inspire reverence.
Tao Qian dwells in refined distinction,
Wei Zhen embodies pure integrity.
Like Lu’s gaze toward heaven’s decree,
Cap and sash await sagely employ.
The maternal hall honors saintly kindness,
Gateways assist in steadfast devotion.

Lu’s rhapsody fears chasing the phoenix,
Jiang’s threads emulate the bear’s omen.
Grand designs merit intricate splendor,
Vast enterprises shine with dazzling light.
Brilliant hues rival lightning’s flight,
Ringed timbers surpass Jiao’s rainbow.
Bound volumes divide steadfast sincerity,
Silken veils adorn the hanging drapes.

Not inferior to Fang’s Penglai feast,
Surpassing Ban’s garden’s toil.
Jade groves connect embroidered chambers,
Jasper trees adjoin pearl palaces.
The eastern sun arrives in vibrant hues,
Southern darkness stirs winged motion.
Jin and Zhang command weighty regard,
Pan and Xie delight in timely harmony.

Vast vistas forget the dusty world,
Flowing sights embrace Mount Hua’s splendor.
A hundred marriages await Gu Yan,
Four virtues shame Wang Rong’s fame.
Han’s blossoms unite in crisp brilliance,
Yin’s washes compose layered art.
Eaves and beams align in dark and white,
Caps and carriages await jade’s luster.

Swallows and sparrows rejoice in deep kinship,
Gardens and ponds abound in lush plenty.
Ancestral blessings extend far,
Successors continue fragrant glory.
Early virtue thrives through prosperity,
Excellent plans unite in accord.
Hesitant steps shame the delayed greeting,
Renewed creation brings joyous growth.

Shaded trees know the grandsons’ care,
Vast texts hope for Ma Rong’s legacy.
Fragrant seasons scatter in fleeting grace,
Auspicious vapors flourish in verdant might.
Often ashamed by my feeble decline,
I only aspire to stand tall.
Books and studies fill my leisure days,
Silk and bamboo express lingering winds.

Ancestral virtue bequeaths mountain-like strength,
Parents’ years delight in youthful vigor.
Illustrious ways endure through generations,
Glorious renown spreads without end.

*Xian Quan Ji, Volume Ten Concludes*
*Xian Quan Ji, Volume Eleven*

**Seven-Law Poems by Zhang Yuchu, the Non-Action Heavenly Master of Mount Qi**

**Poem Presented at the Imperial Banquet in Ningtian Hall on the Sacred Festival**
Heaven unfolds ten thousand years of autumnal clarity,
A hundred lords gaze in reverence, moved by the Sage’s grace.
Golden tablets borne on clouds escort the imperial chariot,
Brocade robes suffused with sunlight gleam upon the palace halls.
Rites performed by inner scribes—fragrant seals draw near,
Music of the palace court resounds with joyous radiance.
This grand ceremony, so noble and profound, shall endure through ages,
Yet I, in humble garb, stand shamed amid such boundless favor.

**Composed Upon Receiving the Imperial Summons to Return to the Mountains on the Twenty-First Day of the Ninth Month, Guiyou Year**
The new pavilion of Xuanpu floats with royal qi,
Swift steeds bear the imperial decree to the celestial court.
The emperor’s words descend from the palace, melting the sunlit day,
Heaven’s guards attend the throne, solemn in autumn’s purity.
In rustic robes, I am permitted to tend pine and chrysanthemum,
How dare I, in lofty rank, compare to phoenix or simurgh?
The emperor’s grace runs deep—what can I offer in return?
With loyal heart, I gaze in reverence at his grand design.

**In Reverent Awe of the Sacred Discourse on the Marvel of Divine Immortals Presenting Elixirs, Which Illuminates the Teachings—Composed in Joy to Record the Event**
The Sage Emperor embodies the Dao, perfecting the subtle net,
From Mount Lu, famed immortals bestow longevity and health.
Even Dongfang Shuo could not monopolize Han Wu’s favor,
While Guangchengzi awaited the Yellow Emperor’s audience.
A thousand springs of crane-like years—cinnabar’s wondrous art,
Ninefold steps before the dragon countenance—jade nectar’s glow.
The imperial words flow gently, filling me with boundless joy,
This humble servant leaps in praise, chanting ever more fervently.

**Early Court on the First Day of Spring**
At dawn, I hasten to the celestial guard to hail the advent of spring,
Delighted to witness the return of yang and the Sage’s renewed virtue.
By chance, I tend flocks where cranes roam the forbidden grounds,
While colored oxen bear dew to the maple hall.
A thousand officials, sashed in jade, raise voices in gladness,
Ten thousand guards, banners unfurled, harmonize the land’s qi.
From this day forth, great harmony shall perfect governance—
I, a rustic from the hills, look up to the imperial decree.

**Accompanying the Sacrificial Rites at the Imperial Ancestral Temple**
Bright torches illuminate the temple gates in solemn splendor,
Jade steps and immortal processions gleam in daylight’s radiance.
The Son of Heaven descends to the ritual vessels and sacred tripods,
The imperial carriage pauses, robes aglow in the sun’s embrace.
Ten thousand guards, banners fluttering, encircle the Phoenix Pavilion,
A thousand officials, plumes aligned, stand in ranks like cranes.
This humble servant, from the wilds, rejoices in the ancestral rites,
May the dynastic succession henceforth tread a path of a hundred blessings.

**Early Court on New Year’s Day, Jisi Year**
Through the fifth watch, morning bells stir the palace gates,
I lift my gaze to the celestial towers, where dawn clouds align.
At the palace wings, jade pendants jingle north of the fragrant carriage,
From the lofty pavilion, bridles chime west of the colored ranks.
Snow’s hue reaches the green-tiled gates in the distance,
Spring’s light stirs the embroidered saddles’ mud.
All pray the emperor’s grace will fall like sweet rain,
While rivers and mountains gain years, moved by the phoenix’s rule.

**Early Court and Imperial Banquet on the Winter Solstice**
The day welcomes the solstice, mild as spring’s return,
Heaven’s guard stands in full display—rites and music arrayed.
The imperial chariot gleams with starlight in the silver candle’s glow,
Jade girdles press against snow, brocade saddles renewed.
Flowers brighten the inner chambers, where green-tiled doors open,
Willows brush the palace robes as they attend the purple throne.
Deeply shamed to join the ranks of egrets and herons,
I share in the joy of the Sage’s virtue spreading pure benevolence.

**Imperial Banquet in the Huagai Hall on the Ninth Day of the Ninth Month, Guiyou Year**
Dawn’s city veiled in mist and rain,
On this auspicious day, the feast begins beneath the emperor’s favor.
Dark halls and damp clouds obscure the grotto paths,
The palace river’s sparse willows fringe the imperial precincts.
Chrysanthemum petals float in palace wine, brimming the cups,
Orchid dew drifts through the courtyard, where garden trees stand sparse.
Ancestral blessings shower me with imperial grace,
In crane robes, I can only feel my unworthiness.

**Imperial Gift of Robes on the Ninth Day**
Twice I have received the emperor’s favor, bestowed with palace robes,
From the jade hall, the decree is proclaimed—I am shamed by such fortune.
Envoys from the imperial wardrobe add feathered pendants,
Honors from the lofty pavilion summon the spirit’s pride.
Fragrant silk gleams in the sun, floating in azure hues,
Light silk sways in the breeze, rippling like green waves.
My devotion to the state must be repaid with utmost sincerity,
May this pure radiance ever adorn my humble station.

**Imperial Gift Received on the Ninth Day of the Tenth Month**
Again, extraordinary grace descends in resplendent decree,
My mountain retreat and terrace halls suddenly shine with glory.
My name, heard at the green-tiled gates, is passed by the chamberlains,
The edict, issued from the yellow doors, appoints me a provincial official.
Rosy clouds steep the wine of the Marshal’s office,
Snow-like flakes pile high with the meat of the imperial kitchen.
Yet I, in rustic garb, know not what I can offer—
I only wish to see the common folk relieved of hunger and want.

**Imperial Gift of Ritual Robes on the Twenty-Seventh Day of the Eleventh Month, Guiwei Year**
The inner eunuch hastens with the decree from the palace of medicine,
Golden robes and rainbow hues—I bow in profound gratitude.
Incense smoke and starry constellations illuminate the three realms,
The imperial procession and windswept clouds face the ninefold gates.
The emperor’s grace, like rain, soaks the land of Yu’s tribute,
His royal way, vast as heaven, sings of Yao’s dominion.
Deeply shamed by my meager worth—what can I add?
Dare I await the bridge’s collapse to pay homage to Red Pine?

**Staying at Chaotian Palace, Presented to Master Wang Dongbai, the Alchemist**
The jade altar touches autumn’s lofty air,
I alone, a mountain dweller, feel shamed among the venerable.
Long vines drape the market gates, jade locks secure,
Dense bamboo surpasses men, golden blades gleam.
At dawn’s rain, I lean on my desk, lost in study,
At dusk’s chill, I regret my lack of a crane robe.
Fortunate to have the Master of Huayang as my neighbor,
A lone crane cries at midnight in the nine marshes.

**Inscribed on *Clouds and Mist Over Myriad Valleys of Fanghu*, a Painting**
The immortal of Fanghu, peerless in sea and mountain spirit,
Accustomed to gathering qi, merging with the vast blue.
Cloudy peaks and distant mists condense in misty hues,
Misty isles and faint ripples echo the distant shoals.
I imagine seeking the grottoes of Lingfeng and Goulou,
Who among the dust-bound kalpas could speak of Mieming?
In vain I sigh for the lofty winds of Mount Song’s solitude—
What are the Eight Steeds compared to the sweat of a thousand miles?

**Mid-Autumn Gathering with Zhou Zhenbai at the Zhanbi Pavilion**
Autumn’s hues divide the equinox, the moon is perfectly round,
In joyful discourse, we share a splendid feast.
Tripods and ritual vessels bear the marvels of Qin’s craft,
Tadpole script preserves the legacy of Han’s calligraphy.
Dew spills fragrant wine, congealing in lustrous beauty,
Lush jade trees stand graceful in the garden’s glow.
Few now remain of the venerable elders of Penglai—
Fortunate to spread pure fragrance and delight in long years.

**Viewing My Old Collection of *Lingpi Jade*, with Thoughts of Its Former Owner**
Mysterious jade, strange peaks nurture numinous essence,
Nine heavens’ clouds and mists arise again at night.
Yanshan’s chamber holds the immortal pearl’s tears,
Wu’s isles and misty waves mingle with the Wei’s streams.
Crane calls often moisten my bookshelf,
Dragon’s radiance at times brightens my inkstone.
The mountain man once aspired to Kongtong’s longevity—
Serene and steadfast, he roots in heaven’s mystery to repay its wonders.

**Inscribed on *Autumn Thoughts in the Cloudy Mountains of Fanghu*, a Painting**
Jade-like peaks stand tall in dawn’s chilly emerald,
Best viewed from the eastern pavilion in tranquil contemplation.
Frost-kissed forests and windblown dew hold pearls’ luster,
Autumn waters and lotus blooms spill like unspooled silk.
Clogs cast aside, I tread the wild paths,
Who now leans on a long pole, angling alone?
From the northern park, my spirit naturally communes—
I am content with these cloudy mountains for my tray of stones.

**Inscribed on *Lofty Depths of Sea and Mountains*, a Painting by Fanghu**

**At the Sea and Mountains Hermitage by Iron Cauldron City,**
The Immortal of the Flask’s noble bearing meets the azure void.
By night, whale-waves spew forth, turning the tide to white;
At autumn’s equinox, the turtle’s back gleams green as Sword Pavilion.

I await the tryst with Qin Gao, who once rode the carp in leisure,
Yet still suspect the spirit of Ji Kang fleeing in haste.
Lord Ying’s home lies by Rainbow Radiance Isle—
Ice and jade at times fill his courtyard and hall.

**Inscribed on a Visit to Zhaozhen Abbey, Presented to Alchemist Master Zhutian**
Disciples of the coiled dragon sound the white flute,
Their stone chambers nestled beside the divine.
Through peaks drenched in rain, I tread at dusk in clogs;
Beyond the ravine, clouds clear as I arrange my books.

The elixir furnace’s glow summons the tiger’s roar,
While thunderous cliffs and winds stir the dragon’s breath.
Yesterday, seeking truth, I woke from wine’s embrace—
In waking and dreaming, I long for you, ever serene.

**Roaming South Mountain Lake**
Orchid oars and cassia paddles glide through secluded depths,
A fleeting true journey reaches the evening’s shade.
Clouds guard the crane’s flight, a single lotus leaf;
Waves rock the dragon isle, its stones a thousand fathoms deep.

Distant peaks hoard the golden and silver qi,
Mystic winds at times waft notes of purple and emerald.
Fortunate to share this transcendent delight,
The mountains’ lingering echoes rest in treasured jade.

**Inscribed on a Scroll of Three Maoshan**
From ancient times, the immortal altar binds Gourd Valley,
The Mao Lords’ halls and pavilions rise amid three peaks.
Divine scriptures cry out from stones, chasing Qin’s inscriptions;
Secret scrolls pass through generations, boasting Han’s seals.

At the feast, the jade pendants chime like spring’s hidden stars;
Damp robes and sword’s qi summon the crimson dragon by night.
I once envied those who read the *Registers of Ascension*—
Would that I might dwell in Huayang, beneath some lone pine.

**Inscribed on the Pavilion of Purity and Whiteness**
Inheriting purity’s legacy, I revere your noble name,
The lofty pavilion embraces the river’s spirit in verdant hues.
Empty azure sashes bind the swift steed at rest,
Kingfisher curtains part to reveal painted screens.

Spring fills the library as clouds reach the seat;
Evening’s wine and poetry shift with the moon across the courtyard.
Ever has loyalty and filial piety graced the virtuous chamber—
In rustic garb, I vainly yearn to behold the Star of Health.

**Inscribed on *Fanghu’s Thatched Hut*, a Painting**
Hills and streams cradle the thatched hut by the river’s bend,
Its limpid radiance captured in shimmering jade-green.
Yan Guang’s fishing shoals make clouds his home;
Wei Yao’s books find stones for neighbors.

Tree hues yield to frost as peaks gather the dusk,
Waterfall’s roar severs the ravine’s spring.
The Immortal of the Flask savors such secluded charm—
How many claim this lofty, solitary wind?

**Inscribed on the White Cloud Pavilion**

**Inscribed on the Pine and Bamboo Pavilion**

Beyond the lordly gates, a detached lodge stands west of the five clouds;
Its limpid groves and valleys rival the crane’s perch.
Moonlight spills over golden balustrades, weighting the drooping willows;
The wind turns silver goblets as fallen blossoms bow low.
A crane-feather cloak gleams like snow, awaiting the tide-borne magpie;
A single peak glows with spring’s dawn, waiting for the crowing cock.
How could lofty joy compare to mountain solitude?
Its radiant splendor vies with heaven’s height.

**Inscribed on the Pine and Bamboo Pavilion**

Noble kinsmen’s towering gates lean on embroidered screens,
Yet pine and bamboo still guard their verdant grace.
Clouds gather round the pavilion, where thatched peaks rise fair;
Snow’s hue invades the gate, where carved waters pause.
Crimson doors and green tassels catch the evening glow;
Broidered saddles and silver candles bear the stars of spring.
How could reclusive longing match the mountain dweller’s taste?
The frost-brushed stone and icy stream ring clear.

**Inscribed on the Hall of Congealed Purity**

Lofty halls rise amid autumn’s emerald trees,
Their pure fragrance swirling to strengthen the divine land.
Flowers congeal in mist, their pendants hanging still;
The wind bears river waves as moonlight fills the tower.
At dusk, the Yellow Chamber echoes the *Parrot’s Rhapsody*;
In spring, the Jade Terrace warms the quail’s heart.
A glorious name delights in outshining the port’s radiance—
In rustic garb, I shame the soaring roc.

**Banquet at the Tranquil Abyss Studio**

We bid the immortal’s pavilion and Fangzhu’s vessel,
True delight—why entrust it to painted scrolls?
Embroidered chambers greet the wind with water-chestnut and algae;
Broidered pillars wear mist like calamus and bulrush.
Feasts unfold in daylight, steaming the valley of rosy clouds;
Terraces overlook autumn waves, threading moonlit pearls.
In my plain robes, I alone blush for my meager fare—
Yet how could bridle and bit yield to Shu Hao?

**A Recluse Presents Two Stalks of Purple Ganoderma**

Towering forests weave jade hues into a numinous form;
An old man from the wilds knows to gather and present them.
Dark mist lifts the branches, transforming them to jasper;
Pure clouds drape like canopies, birthing jade’s marrow.
The Daoist by the clear stream indulges his mountain passion;
The Master of Jiao’s Vale lives untouched by the world’s doubt.
Together we age amid wind and frost in these hills and streams—
Why should auspicious omens shame refined words?

**Visiting the Waterfall Grotto**

A secluded grotto’s twin gates open into boundless dark;
Jade groves cast their shade as we tread in succession.
Tiered cliffs let pearls fall as the curtain draws the cascade;
Layered peaks unfold like brocade, lining the pillars.
I still seek the whistling master to strike the stone;
I long to grasp the vines and await Qiu Sheng.
The crags and slopes lie beneath the forest’s twilight haze—
The zither’s strings pour out the world’s beyond emotions.

**Gathering Jade-Plums Among the Peach Trees**

The peach pool is the immortals’ own planting,
Its branches most beloved where azure seas drip.
Nongyu washes her rouge with mica’s screen;
Feiqiong arranges her brushes on the water nymph’s steps.
A startled wind stirs not the dust of kalpas;
Dew’s touch congeals like snow upon its skin.
Plucked for the mountain window in sleepless quiet,
I seem to hear the sheng’s notes and cranes descending to the curtained study.

**Drinking at the Deep Azure Pavilion: Ode to a Stalactite Cup**

Stalactite wine pours amid flowering herbs,
A flying spring most joyous for the immortal’s home.
It whitens robes like silk by the window;
It reddens cheeks like dawn’s glow, lacking only rosy clouds.
I shame myself for drunken revels like Lun and Yu;
Its literary brilliance befits Zhang Hua.
My fading form still borrows its nurturing strength—
Why seek more on the Double Ninth?

**Inscribed on a Painting of Red Cliff**

How could his mighty prose alone surpass Zhuang and Qu?
Through ages, lofty sentiment reveres his pure fate.
A night moon’s skiff passed Xiakou;
Autumn winds leaned on the wild hut at Lingao.
The legacy of Zhou Lang lingers in the lone crane;
Zhuge’s loyal spirit swells the mighty waves.
I imagine Snow Hall embracing two guests—
The painting awaits a master’s brush to capture its marvel.

**Inscribed on *Meng Haoran Treading Snow***

Beyond Deer Gate’s high seclusion, beyond frost and snow,
He treads the snow, chanting verses with lingering thought.
His poetic spirit naturally rivals Bao and Xie;
His reclusive fame need not match Wang and Zhang alone.
The wild bridge’s chill shallows cradle his tattered hat;
Mountain trees, startled by wind, chase his misty satchel.
Still he holds Meng Pavilion’s ancient intent—
Ink’s sparse glow reveals its faint trace.

**A Recluse Presents a Stone**

The stone elder gladly moves the purple grotto’s clouds;
The recluse unties it from his brocade pouch.
Yin’s essence falls to earth, congealing spring rain;
Water’s foam forms rosy clouds, gathering in daylight’s warmth.
By the rush-woven window, the wind’s length startles magpies;
In the ganoderma chamber, mist’s warmth dreams of stars parting.
Why should mountain folk boil it in the stream?
A refined taste deeply knows to cleanse impurity’s haze.

**Paper Curtains**

Snow-white paper, borne in baskets, writes of silk’s glow;
Square curtains, stitched together, grace the cloud-like bed.
Spring ice warms, stirring heaven and earth’s vastness;
Frost moon’s radiance clears, lengthening the water clock’s drip.
Beyond Mount Hua, dragons lie subdued;
In Zhuangzi’s garden, butterflies fly free.
Originally pure within and without,
Its roots endure winter’s breath across the eight wilds.

**Charcoal in the Brazier**

Stacked firewood’s flames rise to meet the sky,
Defying frost and snow’s bitter cold for all to share.
Its nature hardens through refining, not from blackness;
Its striking sound rings clearer, its glow burns redder.
Wood and metal form images, revealing cinnabar’s hour;
Li and Kan complete the celestial cycle, seizing creation’s craft.
Let not the bellows weary of their task—
Heaven’s mechanism flows through the six voids.

**Inscribed on the *Scroll of Master Dongxuan***

Early I admired the mysterious void, studying nurturing life;
Long I followed the celestial guard, dwelling in the divine capital.
The Great Void is but the primal chaos’ body;
The empty cavern holds the silent, soundless voice.
Clouds and qi often ride distant rosy pendants;
Pine shade ever guards the stone chamber’s purity.
The *Five Thousand Words’* meaning must be fused—
Sitting, I aid the imperial way to answer sagely brightness.

**Visiting Master Lianyi, the Alchemist of Pengshan**

Late elms rise high in the hall’s renewed construction;
A lone bridge spans twin streams in autumn’s clarity.
Wild vines trail the fence, their fading flowers casting shadows;
Round the door, forest pools echo the passing rain.
The orchard’s path winds through yellow-leafed lanes;
The ganoderma gatherer ages beneath white clouds.
I have long planned to visit Pengshan’s master—
For now, I linger in his thatched hut, savoring each moment.

**Inscribed on *Bai Chongyi’s Thatched Hut***

At the Imperial Academy, he transmitted the classics, favored by his lord;
His heart, like mountain valleys, delights in pure radiance.
Short eaves birth white clouds, veiling the chamber;
An old garden congeals the cold, as bamboo screens the door.
Pins and pendants need not flee the palace gates;
Hills and gardens need not wait for the fisherman’s perch.
The forest of words truly holds a retiring spring—
Would that its brilliance might shine upon my indolent robes.

**Presented to Daoist Wang of Mount Mao**

For sixty springs you have dwelt in Huayang,
Your jade tones and resonant chants heard as extraordinary.
White clouds grace your courtyard, where orioles and flowers rest;
Red leaves adorn the forest’s edge, where moon and dew part.
Why need cranes’ backs compose the sheng’s score?
Dragon’s light makes swords inscribe their patterns.
Soon you must chant the empty echoes in the stone chamber—
Yang and Xu’s legacy dispels the world’s haze.

**Inscribed on Mount Taihe**

Taihe’s grandeur coalesces in towering peaks,
Where the Northern Culmen’s sacred winds command worship.
Emerald cliffs warm the clouds, the cinnabar mortar steadfast;
Jade terraces, sparse trees—sword’s light surges.

**By the Western Stream’s Plum Arbor**

Moss-laced paths part beneath the plum arbor’s west,
Banners beyond the heavens guard the Herb Palace.
At the palace gate, you bask in the sovereign’s grace—
Your homeland afar, framed as if by a painter’s art.

**Roaming Peach Blossom Spring**

Spring’s end, the mountain peach’s path grows hard to trace,
Moss carpets the steps, the old house lies deep in shade.
Cliffside cascades echo through the emerald ravine,
Stone gates twist beneath the shade of ancient vines.
Within the clouds, parrots and hounds dwell in the Thunder Chamber,
At the valley’s mouth, fields and orchards skirt Tiger Woods.
Once I lingered two nights in the cinnabar hall,
Vainly inquiring of past traces, idly chanting their rhyme.

**Visiting a Friend at Fanxi Abbey**

Where hills and streams excel, dust’s clamor fades,
The path to Yingzhou leads to seek the hidden sage.
Beyond the gate, wild boats glisten with leaping fish,
Beneath pine shadows, the high pavilion cradles nesting cranes.
At dawn’s first light, I thread through blossoms to enter,
In clear skies, I watch yellow millet swept from the path.
Were it not for an old friend’s enduring pure bond,
Who would hear the lonely longings of my heart?

**Inscribed on *Summer Mountains in Fanghu*, a Painting**

Yue’s most exquisite and lofty, its charm supreme,
A spring-green stream, the boat yet moored.
Clouds link Fanghu’s peaks, summoning cranes,
The sky ends at Min and Emei, where turtles vanish.
An old house rests quietly in the village’s evening haze,
Distant forests stretch, brushed by the rain’s sigh.
Rare now are Jiangnan’s surviving ink traces—
I turn to recall Fang Gan, peerless in his age.

**Paying Homage at the Temple of Marquis Liu**

Once among the feudal states, he held his fief,
The Yellow Stone’s three pacts bestowed their plain writ.
How could Han’s rift compare to the carriage’s return?
The Chu troops had already surrendered, their banners split.
He spoke of pardoning Yong Chi, no grudge held,
Persuaded Han Xin to yield, the false king’s claim undone.
Late descendants bask in his ancestral glory,
Each time I pass the shrine, my heart trembles in awe.

**Roaming the Thunder Altar**

Tigers crouch atop the crag, the stone altar soars,
Wind and thunder rise on all sides from the forest’s edge.
From below, the red dust seems but a crucible of dust,
The sun wheels through the sky like a feathered chariot.
Fragrant trees cling to the cliffs, mist veils the path,
Jade halls and heavenly gates stand in piercing cold.
Seated, I suddenly brandish the Azure Spirit’s sword,
Treading rainbow mists, the cry of cranes and phoenixes rings.

**Roaming Lingzhi Crag**

Parting the mist at dawn, I seek the tiger’s trail,
Leaning on the cliff, the lone rock juts into the void.
Purple lingzhi smokes in warmth, its sacred root endures,
Emerald walls loom deep, the wild path stretches on.
Ancient trees, a thousand years, forget the kalpas’ turn,
A few plum blossoms drift on the wind’s whim.
In the ravine’s mossy steps, traces remain—
Across ages, this pure journey was no mere chance.

**Inscribed on the Pavilion of Lake Light and Mountain Hue**

Jiangdong’s lakes and mountains reign o’er a hundred prefectures,
Here, a worthy governor’s virtue shines.
The official pavilion floats on waters wrapped in sky’s glow,
Lingzhi peaks rise in mist, bathed in moonlight.
Black canopies and new axes herald his governance,
Jade halls bear the legacy of his pure loyalty.
Once, spring sails were moored amid mist and rain—
Still, I long to share this peerless vista with the clouds.

**Inscribed on *Heaven’s Auspicious White Clouds at Sacred Well Mountain***

Once the Golden Immortal dwelt on Dragon-Spout Peak,
Ten thousand acres of white clouds like a sea’s waves.
By night, tigers grew still in the stone ravine,
By day, winds howled in the snow-laden hall.
The vast void’s breath—small as a snail’s horn,
The turbid world’s ten thousand things—light as goose down.
Those who come from the west with gourd and bamboo hat to seek the Dao,
Whose wondrous ink faintly transcends the world’s toil.

**Inscribed on *Fanghu’s Rain-Bringing Bamboo***

Master Fanghu’s spirit roamed the boundless,
His lone surviving ink illuminates a thousand autumns.
Tigers crouch on stone, thunder shakes the earth,
Bamboo scatters rain, phoenixes alight on the mounds.
Sweet rains bring relief, turning back the kalpa’s end,
Sacred texts lie hidden on perilous peaks, in mystic isles.
By ancient pact, he soars beyond the ancients—
Still, his dripping brush leaves jade-green trails.

**Roaming the Divine Tortoise Kingdom of Nanfeng**

Dragons soar, phoenixes gather, shaping ridges and peaks,
The Jade Treasury’s divine legacy, the Crow’s Altar’s swift winds.
Emerald cliffs and jagged peaks face the north,
Green Tortoise Ridge coils eastward in embrace.
Spring conceals the forest valleys, the sky’s light pure,
Sleeves hide wind and thunder, the sword’s chill lingers.
Ashamed, I bear the jade casket as a true heir—
Gazing up, I seek the sacred traces, climbing once more.

**At Huangtang Abbey, Replying to Fellow Travelers**

Urging cranes through the woods, I cross the plank bridge,
The immortal maiden, her hair coiled in fragrant thatch.
Heaven drapes the four wilds with twin-clouded clogs,
Earth dampens the spring sky, rain half-fills the nests.
Green bamboo encircles the curtains, as if tigers lurk beyond,
Purple caskets brim on perilous heights, chasing hidden dragons.
Whose home claims the West Mountain’s finest?
Lend me a branch for my bundled journey.

**Seeking a Retreat at Xianquan’s Mountain Haven**

The immortals’ secluded realm belongs to the Pure Capital—
Dare I choose these woods and hills as my destined home?
Mountain hues already share the dragon ravine’s emerald,
The spring’s voice awaits the crane-court’s missive.
Su Men’s mighty whistle seems to echo near,
Ju Lou’s cinnabar sands are famed for nurturing emptiness.
Heaven bestows white clouds—how dare I be clumsy?
Gladly I’ll follow gourd and bamboo hat, dwelling in humble wine.

**Inscribed on *Mountain’s Radiance and Sea’s Moisture*, a Painting**

The illustrious house of Guanxi’s lineage endures,
By the stream’s pavilion, they dwell east of Chu.
Ten acres of spring clouds swathe the green silkworms,
A courtyard of autumn waters mirrors emerald screens.
The recluse’s joy recalls Pan Yue,
The scrolls’ pure fragrance evokes Ma Rong.
The painted scene seems to capture the farthest seas and peaks—
Still, I seek the ancestral legacy, embracing its flowing grace.

**Autumn Feast at the Foundry**

The sagely sovereign unfurls his chart, halting the six dragons,
The Foundry City’s mountains and peaks coil in grandeur.
Crane pavilions stand twin in the misty glow,
Phoenix paths part the cypress and parasol winds.
Frost-laden jade trees brush sleeves with green,
Newly poured jade cups glow on crimson faces.
Drunken verses draw near the immortals’ realm—
Together we revere the rare favor of feasting in the Herb Palace.

**Longing for Xianquan**

A lone peak coils with stone, a record of quiet sway,
Wind and dust’s steps—dreams never stray.
Clearing the wilds, a thatched eave faces the evening marsh,
Hoeing the misty stone steps, they charm the cold glow.
Half the grove’s flowered rain thins in spring’s shade,
A ravine’s lingzhi clouds dim the Dao’s trace.
How many days till autumn skies turn yellow?
Still, I suspect the clear night finds me seated on the mossy isle.

**To the Daoist Recorder of Toxic Affairs**

Joyfully I watch the cyclical years complete their round,
Nurturing the true self, fittingly lingering in the capital.
Peach blossoms ripen before spring, mist drapes the robe,
Winter solstice’s plum blooms, dew fills the cup.
In the grand court, pure inquiries surpass Yan Si,
In the inner canon, profound discourse excels Chuqiu.
Our recent parting swiftly becomes a cloud’s divide—
I can only pray for your longevity of eight thousand autumns.

**Gazing at Lingzhi Clouds by the Spring**

White clouds have long nested in the valley,
Loving the mountain spring’s likeness to nurturing obscurity.
Heaven narrows the door and courtyard, barely a canopy’s bow,
Earth divides the luminous peaks, small as a drawn bow.
Good fields border the wilds, like Zhuge’s,
Fine mushrooms rise in rows, after Lu Tong’s.
Beside the clouds, purple lingzhi may be eaten—
No need to seek the solitary phoenix in the mortal world.

**Banquet in the Snow with Daoist Master Miao**

In Xuan Du’s brocade hall, a feast in the Western Pure,
Daylong snow swirls, auspicious hues gleam bright.
Immortal wine, warmed, turns clouds to emerald green,
Cave plums bloom before year’s end, jade petals drift in mist.

Keen winds part the frost at the phoenix-crested gate,
Visiting bamboo, crane-adorned rails line the hall.
Ashamed, my rustic steps intrude this noble gathering—
May distant years bring you boundless honor and grace.

---

**Inscribing the Painting *Autumn Wind over Fang the True Man’s Thatched Hut***

Whose house stands by the boulder-lined fishing cove?
Light ink plays on the tranquil grove’s canvas.
The numinous zither’s damp notes summon distant cranes,
Petal shade slows our steps, sharing gulls’ ease.

Autumn wind ages the hut—Yang Xiong’s old abode,
Flowing water hums at the gate—Xie Tiao’s mountain.
Where my virtue pales ‘mid bamboo’s chill and river’s jade,
Gazing at the scroll, my dreams take flight once more.

---

**On the Fourth Day of the First Month, Receiving the Edict to Return to the Mountains: Parting from Immortal Attendant Fu**

For months, awe weighed on me in the bamboo palace,
Now the Emperor’s grace, profound, bids me return.
The Dipper’s rays weave through rosy clouds,
The Kunpeng’s head bears moonlit dew.

Clearing snow bridges the spring-crossing rain,
Warm clouds trail the evening tide’s breeze.
Raising my cup, parting sorrow deepens—
May crane-longevity and tortoise-years be ours to share.

---

**Parting from Daoist Master Zi**

Snow clears as we meet, laughing in our jade carriage,
Jade terrace’s spring rivals the hall’s splendor.
Qinhuai’s waters swell with the spring tide,
Wu trees’ mist fades in sparse night rain.

The immortal bureau’s purple sable trails cloud-steps,
River sails and black caps blur in misty huts.
Half a year’s parting divides us from forest and spring—
I’ll refine the elixir, seeking the brocade-cliff texts.

---

**Winter Days in Mountain Retreat**

Warm sun bathes the day in radiant glow,
Empty hills, pond’s edge—carved doors stay shut.
White clouds, cushioned, share the woodcutter’s path,
Purple cave’s folk return, dogs guarding their way.

Snow tea’s froth surges, then the spring runs thin,
Pine-brewed dew-wine—few guests now remain.
Leisure stirs me to hasten the plum’s bloom,
Soon the valley will be all emerald hues.

---

**Composing at Mountain Retreat on the Third Day of the Third Month**

In the world, I shame my fleeting traces,
Yet in the mountains, days pass in pine-wind ease.
Dragon well’s water swells, clouds steam the mist,
Forests bow like whale waves, veiling the sky.

Pool’s algae sways, hooks part the near green,
Cliff flowers cling to clogs, treading fading red.
Fleeting glory—why vie for gourds’ tether?
Wine in hand, joy transcends the mortal realm.

---

**Winter’s Clear Day: Seeking the Former Site of Hunlun Hermitage**

Staff in hand, I wander the valley’s depths,
Silent, the pipa stream’s path runs deep.
Fields and plains stretch, winding and secluded,
Grass and brambles mark the ruins’ rugged trace.

Sun-warmed slopes melt frost on the path,
Wind-swept steps chill the tiger-haunted grove.
Who grasps Hunlun’s ancient intent?
Only pines and wutong keep the years’ heart.

---

**Inscribing the Painting *Fanghu’s Return to the Hut***

Fanghu’s brush blurs the vast and hazy,
Mirage-like, the linked huts share the ore’s fate.
Beyond form and qi, the cosmos is seen,
Great vistas of rivers and peaks dwell in being and non-being.

Frosted forests, leopard mists—autumn’s voice lingers,
Misty isles, dragon pools—sea hues merge.
Where to seek the Jiang and Han?
Unashamed, the secluded valley cradles Fang Peng’s rest.

---

**Gazing After Emperor Yu at the Former Sites of Jinye Hermitage and Tianrui Hermitage**

Golden immortals’ wondrous structures tread Kunlun,
Tianrui once glimpsed the *Yu gong*’s texts.
Mountain breath melts spring, scattering mist,
Heaven’s light lingers in snow, casting day’s shade.

Swords fly from Liaomei, dust stirs in the kalpa,
Cinnabar guards the abyss, dragons stand peerless.
Through the ages, pavilions blend with wind and moon—
Who now hears the Dao in a single draught of the sacred spring?

---

**Returning to Xian Spring in the Snow**

Mountains heaped with snow flank the stream’s edge,
My staff seeks the old path, untrodden by men.
Jade trees’ broken boughs sprawl on the earth,
The Milky Way’s floating silk threads the frozen rite.

Wind topples nest-cranes, clouds darken early,
Ice scatters cliff-pines, the valley stirs with spring.
In the lofty pavilion’s bitter cold, high repose—
Why seek the mortal world’s phosphorescent isles?

---

**Hermitage**

Long have I cherished reclusion’s joy,
Fleeting fame—now and then, a mere whisper.
In motion, I watch wind and clouds seal the pass,
In stillness, I peer at heaven and earth from my lotus hut.

I’d summon Bao Jing’s pair of swallows,
Weary of chasing Wang Qiao’s twin suns.
Ever grasping the great vision beyond form and qi,
The silent true master reveals the dark pearl.

---

**Inscribing the Hall of Mystic Contemplation**

The eastern ravine’s high hall opens another realm,
Cleansed of dust and grime, it savors the profound.
In the yellow center, observing wonders, I know emptiness’s peak,
In white’s embrace, dwelling in integrity, I grasp the primal image.

Nesting cranes ride the wind, flutes echo the moon,
Stream gulls skim snow, oars part the spring.
The venerable master, once a guest at the Golden Gate,
Early inherits his family’s legacy, joining the immortals’ ranks.

---

**Night Lodging at the Abbey of the Mystic Capital**

Twenty years’ dusty traces—now I return,
The immortal terrace’s marble steles mourn the kalpa’s ashes.
Distant cranes at night’s end first warn of dew,
Abyssal fish in spring’s warmth already startle at thunder.

The stream’s voice remains the peach-blossom waters,
Moonlight still invades the bamboo-leaf cup.
Unworthy heir to the ancestral legacy,
I grieve the rise and fall of wormwood and weeds.

---

**Morning in Flowers: Lodging at the Eastern Peak Palace**

The Eastern Peak’s temple, the Wood Emperor’s shrine,
On this fine day, I ascend in spring’s warmth.
Flowers brighten the mountain county, plains and streams fair,
The divine precinct’s armor and helmets stand mighty.

The Silver Maiden’s shrine laments filial devotion,
The Azure Crow’s tomb marks enduring merit.
May auspicious omens, age after age, govern the realm—
I watch the fleeting light in the moonlit night.

---

**Visiting Stone Immortal Abbey**

Deep into the peach-blossom spring, a hundred acres bloom,
Cinnabar cliffs and jade walls bear dragon veins.
Forms return to the imageless, not gold nor stone,
The land’s numinous essence crowns the misty clouds.

Slanted Dipper’s light joins the cinnabar cavern’s fire,
Crossed boughs’ dampness guards the moss’s patterns.
Delighted to share the carriage’s canopy in true appreciation,
Together we cleanse the dust’s grime in the immortal’s home.

---

**Visiting the Wondrous Spirit Abbey on Turtle Hill by the River**

The immortal terrace coils, overlooking the river’s flow,
The winding path’s secluded source welcomes my return.
Departed cranes trace the Milky Way’s route,
The sacred turtle still dwells on Fenglin Isle.

Five Cities shift the kalpa, cinnabar light stirs,
Three Isles blend spring, jade qi surrenders.
Henceforth, the mystic terrace’s splendor grows—
Lofty winds, generation to generation, spread the true Dao.

---

**Visiting Mount Magu**

Wind-swept steps ascend, a hundred turns distant,
The perilous pavilion embraces the earth, soaring far.
Leaning on emptiness, the silver river’s waterfall cascades,
Flanking the path, secluded bamboos drift in emerald mist.

The dusty realm fades into hillocks,
The immortal capital’s ethereal vastness dawns bright.
Twenty years of travels—all forgotten—
Why seek the true in the vast and empty?

---

**The Celestial Maiden of Gushe Descends to the Five Cities**

The Jade Altar’s winding path ascends into the azure void.

**The Celestial Maiden of Gushe Descends to the Five Cities (continued)**

Arrayed in gossamer robes, she arrives with Wang Yuan beneath the moon,
Her alchemical staff aligned with the heavens, awaiting Cai Jing.
Jade pendants linger where dragon-wells hold snow,
Pavilion beams gleam where Magpie Bridge’s stars sway.

Her steadfast virtue, though erased through a thousand years, still illumines her fragrant steps,
This land of numinous splendor fittingly shelters the hundred spirits.

**Roaming the Crimson Clouds Grotto-Heaven**

An empty cavern conceals the Lesser You in its depths,
Old wanderings and relics stir memories of passing years.
The mountain winds along the raven’s path, coiling through cloud-wreathed steps,
A dragon’s embrace cradles the spring, cascading over stone.

Moss-clad steles stand in fading sunlight,
Sparse woods and carved pavilions overlook the chill mist.
I linger, half-expecting a cloud-feeder’s wild joy,
Yet no jade flute’s notes reach my seat.

**Gazing at Mount Lu’s Snow from a Boat**

On the river islet, a skiff basks in abundant moonlight—
Mount Lu’s spring-cleared peaks rise jagged and grand.
Within Incense Burner Peak, clouds blanket a thousand acres,
At Starlet Bay’s head, snow drifts across slopes.

The wind hushes Tiger Stream’s pure rapids,
Clouds veil the Dragon Chamber as night tides pass.
The white of settled nests blurs with lofty summits,
Carved by spring’s voice to brew stone hollows.

**Offering the Jiao Ritual at the Upper Clarity Palace on the Lantern Festival, Delighted by Clear Skies**

Rain drenched the verdant spring, veiling the sacred rite,
Then suddenly the Lantern Festival’s moon shone full again.
Crane Mountain’s spring fills Kongtong’s feast,
The Celestial Pole’s winds clear the azure heavens’ banquet.

Lotus blooms stream radiance like golden balls,
Heavenly flowers scatter hues like jade maidens.
Rejoicing in the sage’s grace and profound virtue,
The era’s prosperity is inscribed in the almanac of great abundance.

**In Gratitude for the Jiao Ritual’s Completion, Responding to Ge Weizhen**

Old tales speak of your noble house’s imperial favor,
Jade towers now stand even more resplendent and pure.
From afar, I hear the grotto’s ritual hymns entwined with rosy clouds,
Still imagining the immortal terrace’s brocade-laden feast.

Jewel trees by your pillow glow with flickering light,
Jade peaks at your window weave graceful lines.
Ge Hong sips cinnabar-infused water,
While the useless tree finds joy in long years.

**Matching Rhymes with Instructor Shen**

The Jade Capital’s terraces bloom with peach blossoms,
The Heavenly Capital’s steps are trod without weariness.
From the Dragon Pool, we ladle clouds’ hues,
The Rabbit’s brush pales beside the moon’s ink.

Your poetic spirit rivals Shen Yue’s,
Your transcendence evokes Qin Gao’s zither.
When will we meet again, white-haired and parted?
Brewing the elixir’s waters, we revel in eternal joy.

**To Daoist Recorder Cao**

Ancestral blessings endure, revered through past and present,
Yet my fragmented talent grieves the times most deeply.
Fleeting glory aligns with Zhuangzi’s wisdom,
Who peers into Master Zhong’s heart?

Before the parrot cup, spring dreams fade,
By the partridge’s nest, rustic passions roam.
Fortunate to have a trusted friend on the path,
In retreat, I long for your kind words.

**Visiting the Yanfa Abbey on a Fine Day**

The abbey’s pavilions pierce the heavens, jade qi afloat,
Leaning on clouds, they lodge beside the ancient cinnabar mounds.
Frost-chilled bells traverse pine and mist beneath the moon,
Fireflies and crickets trace the autumn’s stone ravine.

Unsurprised that no Wei Bao sweeps my gate,
Most joyful to craft lines like Yang Xiu’s.
A small cup before the lamp deepens our bond,
At dawn, I linger longer at Lingyan’s peaks.

**Ascending Mount Wanshou**

Beyond sheer cliffs, layered peaks emerge from rain and mist,
Winding cloud-steps lead toward the azure vault.
The Flowery Source’s hidden ford swells with silver waves,
Cliffside waterfalls hang like mighty white silk.

At heaven’s edge, cranes’ nests beckon Xu Mai,
Amid perilous heights, I seek Maosong’s alchemical treasures.
Passing the courtyard, I hear of wind and thunder’s charge—
Best to apply wondrous skill upon the lofty summit.

**The Beaded Curtain Pavilion**

A beaded curtain hangs in the small pavilion’s spaciousness,
Night merges with clouds, lodging at the eaves.
Forests hold layered mists, startling as a prowling leopard,
Gullies rush with winds, poised to descend like simurghs.

Orchid curtains glow, dispelling the day’s warmth,
Lanterns’ oil murmurs, hastening spring’s chill.
Idly they speak of Xu Fu gazing toward Penglai’s isles—
Why seek jade terraces for feathered wings?

**Inscribed on Xiao Shi’s Phoenix Terrace**

A perilous terrace soars a hundred feet, crowning the layered heavens,
A rainbow phoenix wheels through the sky, jade pipes attuned.
Xiao Shi’s love was no mortal match,
Nongyu’s immortal nature truly bore heaven’s mark.

Five-cloud towers and pavilions merge with rosy clouds,
Three Isles’ banners drift through mist and dew.
The secret archives offer ample leisure for pure delight—
Autumn’s skies beckon lingering echoes to be summoned.

**Inscribed on the Flying Immortal**

The immortal’s traces fade, yet the painted hues remain vivid,
Floating clouds and empty caverns dissolve into the azure void.
Jade maidens’ pendants flutter where peaches ripen,
Golden mothers pause where bamboo dew gleams.

A light boat bears inscriptions, troubling the crow messenger,
A fragrant seal holds no words, crossing the simurgh’s plow.
The immortal’s roots find harmony in rosy clouds,
Awaiting the legacy of Fang and Cai at the descending court.

**Inscribed on the *Clouds Rising from the Mountain’s Waist* by Fanghu**

The immortal Fanghu’s wondrous ink surpasses Shangyan’s,
Endlessly weaving long forests, ever enraptured.
Clouds break from the mountain’s belly, congealing in dawn’s indigo,
New waters swell at the ravine’s head, steaming in crystalline haze.

Soaring, one seems to hear simurghs’ cries,
Sweeping the path, only dusters’ whispers remain.
Yet rejoice—immortal courts teem with officials,
Gazing outward, emerald hues cling to spring robes.

**Inscribed on the *Gazing at the Sea* Painting**

A boundless expanse of blue-green waves stretches wide,
