Heaven and earth are but a horse—who discerns their bounds?
Mountains invite broad contemplation, revealing clarity,
Courtly plans suffice to secure peace.

Rain clears, island barbarians float across the eight poles,
The moon rises, misty trees link to the Three Hans.
High sentiments are not exhausted by mere paintings—
I laugh and cast my fishing line toward the giant turtle.

**Inscribed on the *Three Gorges* Painting**

A renowned stronghold guards the long Yangtze,
The brocade waters flow west, their course vast and distant.
The heavenly moat’s legacy evokes Du and Ge,
The people’s enduring customs praise Gong and Huang.

Wu Gorge’s beauty mirrors the rope bridge’s distance,
Witch Gorge’s clouds stretch to Sword Pavilion’s length.
When shall we pledge to gaze upon ancestral blessings,
Seeking autumn’s fragrance where flowers are washed?

**The Grand Plough**

The great unity governs the four seas in spring,
At the southern suburb, the emperor’s rites are solemn and sincere.
Stellar avenues bear golden tally-staffs,
Heavenly gates welcome jade chariots.

Jade tablets and bi disks gleam with rosy clouds, honoring Zhou’s classics,
Pendants and seals embrace clouds, renewing Han’s rites.
Alone, I feel shame in my dark robes as I present offerings—
The sage’s virtue and auspicious omens revere the One.

**Ascending Great Mao Peak**

Juqu’s perilous peak crowns the nine heavens,
At dawn, I part rosy clouds to ascend at daybreak.
Below, the vast earth’s banners of mist draw near,
Above, the vaulted sky’s canopy of haze gathers.

Already I embrace Mao’s staff, arriving by feathered carriage,
Still I await Wang and Xu to welcome the numinous tally.
Rejoicing in the new structure soaring into the void,
From here, the true Dao’s winds will spread for a hundred generations.

**Second Mao Peak**

The Dark Continent’s small hollow winds in coils,
Among clustered peaks, the supreme abode stands as the imperial seat.
Eightfold numinous texts mark the jade registers,
Fivefold wondrous traces adorn the jade books.

Dew drifts with celestial lotus, heavenly flowers blaze,
Clouds embrace the imperial carriage, earth’s breaths unfold.

**In Search of Truth**

I long to seek the true and trace lost scriptures,
On Golden Peak’s winding stones, I tread the void.

**Third Peak**
Sheer cliffs plunge into azure depths,
Tengzi Peak winds round the Five Cities’ halls.
Lu’s horse leaves traces in sword-qi’s glow,
Tao and Liu’s fragrant steps echo in pines’ sighs.
Stars hang o’er jade trees above a thousand ravines,
Rocks rise with crystalline blooms encircling four pillars.
Tonight, the jasper altar awaits the full moon—
I shall ride the wind, chasing phoenix and crane.

**To Lecturer Shen of White Clouds**
I recall our parting in the capital’s longing,
By chance in Juqu, I sought your cinnabar shoulder.
In endless forests, I met Red Pine’s immortal,
On Kongtong, why doubt White Stone’s sage?
Alone on the ridge, clouds rise with startled tigers’ roars,
On Jun Mountain, winds howl as deer cry.
Ever since Shen Yue’s poetic thoughts,
We spoke through the night, gazing at the moonlit pavilion’s clarity.

**Staying at Mao Mountain on the Lantern Festival**
Often I wished to seek the reclusive, visit feathered officials,
By chance on the Lantern Eve, I feasted at Kongtong.
Yang’s forest veils the moon o’er terraces,
Mao’s grottoes deepen with cypress and wutong winds.
Drums and songs on Ao Mountain recall old friends,
Rosy clouds and crane steps wander east and west.
Floating dust and worldly affairs stir many feelings—
I gaze high o’er the realm, smiling.

**Roaming Huayang Grotto-Heaven**
Jade pillars coil eastward in piled snow’s guise,
Hollowed stone chambers stretch, elusive to peer.
Only the numinous zither carries pure echoes,
Admitting empty brightness to illumine another dawn.
Clouds gather, startling as snow-windowed paths,
Winds wail, chiding the celestial pool’s drums.
I long to explore the moon’s cavern, summoning yellow cranes—
Wang and Xu’s traces remain, unquestioned.

**Inscribed on Spring Radiance Tower**
The layered tower looms o’er ten thousand homes in spring,
Dawn’s sunlight gleams on jasper halls.
Northern halls’ daylilies lie far from ice and snow,
Han’s splendor binds the pavilion in fresh paintings.
Nine heavens’ crane carriages race through azure gates,
Eight poles’ simurghs descend on brocade wheels.
The imperial screen upholds supreme filial piety—
I await the honor’s gleam in silken decrees.

**Lodging at Wudang’s Side Peak**
One night in the jade temple’s highest peak,
Winding stone steps fade into the empty sky.
Six Ao isles and islets float with golden grains,
Ten thousand horse peaks girdle jade rainbows.
Xuanwu’s banners fly north of the Yellow Road,
Purple Tenuity’s towers stand amid Green Blossoms.
Delighted, the tiger-browed elder’s immortal form—
Beneath the moon, he summons me on crane-back winds.

**Inscribed on Cloud Forest, Springs, and Stones**
The clear stream bears the illustrious lineage’s old renown,
Westward, Cloud Forest’s Sword Pavilion lies athwart.
Verdant ramparts array the skies, floating through kalpas,
Azure voids wash dew, emerging from vast seas.
Wondrously probing the numinous peaks, preserving the central valley,
The Dao aids the mysterious pivot, halting at the upper capital.
I wish to carve thirty-six beloved peaks—
Yet should springs and stones not pledge fragrant vows?

**Inscribed on Immortal Zhou’s Prayer-for-Rain Scroll**
Truly a crane-borne immortal from Su Terrace,
He governs drought relief across the divine realm.
A Xiang’s carriage stirs dark crystal veins,
The Weaving Maid’s loom inverts Taiye’s springs.
Withered lands revive through sacred virtue,
Abundance is offered by numinous decree.
The literary forest rejoices, praising his beauty—
Fertility follows, celebrating great harvests.

**Inscribed on My Portrait**
What talent in the mysterious lineage revives later fragrance?
Early in study, I discerned conduct and concealment.
Two courts’ favor transmitted through azure gates,
Eight memorials’ solemnity arrayed in green documents.
Pines and chrysanthemums chant amid night’s snow,
Cranes and gibbons rest at the valley’s mouth in autumn frost.
Why paint this illusory form in cinnabar and ink?
Through vast kalpas, I shall gaze toward the great wilds.

**Mid-Autumn**
I recall the jade temple’s night, the air so clear,
Again I see autumn’s hues, bowing in gratitude.
Friends’ bonds and letters accumulate,
In the capital’s parting, wine wearies the cup.
Before the seat, I bear the weight of human cauldrons,
In court robes, I still feel the lightness of kingfisher silks.
Deeply favored, how can I repay?
Sleepless, I hear the palace clepsydra’s drip.

**Congratulating Immortal Zhou on Answered Snow Prayer**
The inner court’s yellow hemp descends to a near minister,
The sagely heart longs to blanket the people in snow.
Six-petaled flowers transform kalpas, melting a thousand trees,
Eight scenes’ celestial chapters turn myriad weights.
Silver candles’ glow floats on jade’s vast expanse,
Jasper terraces’ sounds stir emerald phosphorescence.
The literary forest’s praises surpass Mei and Ma—
Together we rejoice in the Dark Capital’s renewed favor.

**Visiting Master Du’an**
On a clear spring day, ten days deep,
I trace winding paths south of the city to the Chan grove.
Lotus-carved clepsydras reveal the true nature of suchness,
Palm-leaf lamps transmit the ancient Buddha’s heart.
Crows’ pagodas hang inverted, mirroring halls’ shadows,
Rainbow pools embrace cypress and pine’s shade.
Master Yuan has long been graced by imperial light—
He permits our poetic covenant to seek again.

**Matching Master Du’an’s Rhymes**
One oar hastens lightly as a crane,
Delighted to meet the Chan patriarch in the divine capital.
Five lamps’ wisdom swords guard mountain spirits,
A thousand Buddhas’ mud pearls startle the ocean’s treasury.
Spring replaces crow nests, washing bamboo,
Rain clears the vegetarian bell, passing plantain mats.
Tea and melons surpass Linji’s flavors—
As poetry’s courier, I console rustic feelings.

**Light as clouds, my paired sandals arrive,**
Long graced by imperial light, dwelling in Haojing.
Dharma rain flies, hiding tigers’ roars,
Scriptures’ flowers fill, startling reclining dragons.
Literary giants surpass Pei and Bai,
Histories’ mighty cries exhaust Xu and Jing.
Beyond the world, allies in this sagely age—
Chan’s subtleties freely cleanse idle thoughts.

**Matching Alchemist Ge’s Rhymes on the Imperial Robe**
In spring’s first month, the year begins,
At dawn, I await the court’s steps, emulating grotto immortals.
Ninefold sacrifices resound with great protection,
Cloudy harmonies’ eight melodies hear Heaven’s music.
Yin’s banner heralds Xia’s jade charts,
Jia’s records transmit Zhou’s precious calendar.
The rustic is repeatedly favored—
Should I recall Yuan and Qi by bamboo and wutong?

**My humble talents have long shamed high peaks,**
How could fleeting fame move the sagely heart?
Inner brews repeatedly bear cauldron’s beauty,
Court robes still feel lotus and water-chestnut’s depth.
I explore Huang-Lao, pondering the "Mysterious Fu,"
Governance harmonizes with Xuan-Yao’s "Striking the Earth" hymns.
Returning to forests and springs, I speak with elders—
The Phoenix Pool’s pure dreams linger still.

**The Terrace of Peace’s cap and sash array Zhou’s ranks,**
New palace decrees embody the Supreme Emperor.
Crowns and talents unite Guan and Yue,
Silken decrees’ literary splendor surpasses Ban and Yang.
Golden chambers await the dawn, gazing beside Heaven,
Jade strategies attend the emperor’s side.
The mysterious hemp’s lineage bears Xuan Hall’s weight—
Your talents should not yet invoke Feng Tang.

**Matching Alchemist Dong’s Congratulatory Rhymes**
From the lattice, joy in great years,
Ascending Penglai, I dare claim second to the immortals.
At the palace gate, I await the dawn in the silken bureau,
In the secret pavilion, I chant at the wooden heavens.

**The Tiger Guards array the heavens, encircling the gyrfalcon’s locks,**
**Dragon robes gleam in the sun, listening to the wild swans’ transmission.**
How could an outer minister suffice to aid the imperial destiny?
Yet the gracious mandate is bestowed anew beside the sun-angled brow.

The divine land’s beauty surpasses the board-like winds of the peaks,
The seasonal signs of yang’s unfolding meet the emperor’s heart.
Snow fills Jianzhang Palace, delighting in the late clearing,
Rain disperses on Taiye Pond, awakening to spring’s depth.

Ashamed to indulge in the recluse’s *Quail and Bustard* ode,
I wish to offer the worthy minister’s *Cricket* hymn.
Should I blame Dong’s springtime for its quiet retreat?
Each time I fail the praise thrust upon me, now and again.

Several times I’ve accompanied the heavenly ranks in a thousand rows,
Illuminating sacrifices with sincerity alongside the Nine August Ones.
I shamefully bear the idle fame of iron cudgels,
My talents fall short of the fixed price, shamed by green poplars.

The official robe, granted by day, soars beyond wind and cloud,
The forbidden banners often bathe beside rain and dew.
Returning, I cherish the elders vying to extol its splendor,
With forests and springs, we together emulate the joy of Yu and Tang.

---

**Matching the Previous Rhymes in Reply to Alchemist Wang (Three Poems)**

**I.**
The precious reign unfolds in a year of great abundance,
The court’s ranks often behold feather-robed immortals.
Spring melts the shell-palace, brightening a thousand pheasants,
Snow clears the jade steps, opening the eight heavens.

The imperial edicts, secretly borne, weigh heavy as the Golden Horse,
The reverent voices are at times heard, transmitted from the Stone Canal.
The manifest gaze of sagely transformation flows to the wild frontiers—
No need for bronze tallies to hasten the border’s vigil.

**II.**
Woodcutters and fishermen long rely on the jade-like peaks,
The sagely lord, at ease, examines the plain heart.
Abundant favors repeatedly bestowed, grasping jade with solemnity,
Exceptional grace descends anew, doubling in depth.

The rites and music of Yu’s court transform through the *Guan Ju*,
The robes and caps of Han’s court chant the *Liang Fu* hymn.
In rustic remoteness, I can only shame myself for offering no inch of aid,
Yet I still aspire to self-cultivation, to fragrance in this age.

**III.**
For five nights, the altar’s legacy arrays the rows of crows,
Yang’s return heralds the seasonal signs of the bound sovereign.
Sincerity reaches the seas and mountains, consulting the divination slips,
My office, secondary to the revered vessels, shames the planted poplars.

The horses of Mei and Ma link their fragrance beside the imperial carriage,
Xiao and Cao follow in the footsteps of the tattered-robed ones.
Mount Wei has long belonged to Wang Qiao’s repose,
The poetic rhythms ever aspire to surpass the two Tangs.

---

**Inscription on the *Dragon and Tiger Mountain* Painting**
The Dao’s realm, past and present, shines east of the river—
Tiger-crouched, dragon-soaring, ten thousand ravines in majesty.
Purple and emerald peaks rise beyond the Three Isles,
Golden and silver terraces stand amid the five clouds.

Heaven lowers its crimson standards, arriving with the Yellow Stone,
Earth bows beneath the jasper banners, awaiting the Red Pine.
Oars stilled, pennants unfurled, I indulge in the ascent,
Unrolling the painting—why seek Penglai’s distant isles?

---

**The Dao’s Precincts, a Mountain of Immortals**
The dark capital’s domain, a mountain of transcendents,
Jade-green waters and cinnabar cliffs encircle the four vistas.
Ten thousand apertures scrape the sky, clamoring with earth’s breath,
Nine heavens’ flying pendants pay homage at the celestial gate.

Cinnabar’s glow by night kindles the leaping dragon of Li,
Sword’s aura by day pursues the returning feathered cranes.
Delighted to receive the numinous canon, I explore Yu’s cave—
In the grand court, I long to speak of its hidden murmurs.

---

**Inscription on the *Sun Kang Studying by Snowlight* Painting**
Accumulated yin flies as sleet from the jade terrace,
The four treasuries’ hanging curtains leave the day unopened.
The great earth’s jasper blossoms gleam where light finds a gap,
Half the sky’s jade trees contend, free of dust.

At Shanyin, straw sandals hinder the search for bamboo,
In the official chamber’s thatched window, I face the plum like a companion.
Through the ages, lofty winds deepen my admiration—
The snow’s lingering blessings rejoice in abundant talent.

---

**Reascending Mount Taihua**
Thrice I sought the lofty immortal on the ten-thousand-*ren* peak,
Climbing and ascending a hundred turns to reach the layered void.
Stars hang from the flowery canopy beyond the azure vastness,
Heaven meets the curved array amid the boundless green.

Nearby, I emulate Mei and Yue, donning feathered pendants,
From afar, I summon Yang and Xu, treading the cool wind.
The true way through the ages equals the mountains and peaks,
The dark grace—

---

**Inscription on the *Dongxiao Palace***
The celestial pillar’s pearl palace spans the sea’s vastness,
From Yu Hang, another path beckons for ascent.
The White Mao Cave hides tigers amid the clouds,
The Green Peak’s mountain stands empty beneath the moon’s simurghs.

Cups float on the lake’s waves, a thousand acres of blue,
Gourds overturn the spring’s flow, nine heavens’ chill.
Gazing at the painting, I indulge in soaring thoughts—
Lying down, I wash away the summer’s dust, hanging up my cap.

---

**Ascending the *River Diagram* Immortal Altar**
The immortal lord’s sacred mound has lost its former palace,
The *River Diagram*’s legacy guards the many peaks.
Southward, I gaze at the sea and mountains, cherishing autumn pendants,
Northward, I recall the wind and clouds, remembering the dawn bell.

The moonlit night’s shadow returns to the ornate pillar’s crane,
The dawn clouds’ light stirs the Ge Pond’s dragon.
Worldly passions shift like past dreams,
The vast kalpa’s numinous terrace—far, I cannot follow.

---
**End of *Xianquan Collection*, Scroll Eleven**
**Beginning of *Xianquan Collection*, Scroll Twelve**

**Seven-Character Long Song: The Song of Mi Yaoshi**
*Composed by Zhang Yuchu, the Non-Action Heavenly Master of Qishan*

The Great Void boundless, vast and profound—
Who first carved the signs of yin and yang’s divide?
The august True Sovereign wields the pivot of transformation,
Stirring, exhaling, turning the key within the moth-eaten lock.
All ten thousand beings share a single source,
Jade tablets and sacred scrolls guard the arcane.
The Mysterious Origin Sage-Ancestor unlocked the wondrous mechanism,
A million subtle words revealed to the empty vastness.
Vast and formless, ere heaven and earth arose,
Nameless, imageless—all was spontaneity.
Refined a hundred times, essence-gold returns to true liquid,
Dragon and tiger, crow and hare entwine in embrace.
Since ancient times, such perfect adepts were rare,
The Perfected One’s treasures passed down through kalpas untold.
Zhurong’s descendant received the strange doctrine,
Barefoot in hempen robes, he knocked at the Thunder Cave.
He claimed to command the opening and closing of rain and sun,
Wielding the thunderbolt’s whip, driving them with fierce might.
In youth, he strode through the Golden Horse Gate,
Great elders and meritorious ministers all bowed in admiration.
Yet he cast off the shackles of cap and sash,
Riding the wind and thunder straight to Wu and Yue.
At that time, gold and jade adorned the heroes,
Who could have foreseen the dust of the world would plunge them into despair?
Vernal splendor before their eyes turned to ashes,
Proudly they spurned the fragrant paths, discoursing at will.
Returning, they at last beheld the True Lord’s face,
Longing to linger in Immortal Crag and Ghost Valley.
Sweeping blossoms, pouring water, they played the pure flute,
Worldly cares and vulgar thoughts never touched them.
From the cave’s perspective, comings and goings are not worth counting—
Ascend my stone steps, wash your ears, and listen to the murmuring stream.
Yesterday’s words suddenly recall my native land,
The Heavenly Crown Altar long lay overgrown and abandoned.
Carved eaves and painted beams—what labor they cost!
Yet after years, the former vision stands mighty once more.
Carving through twin cliffs, the Emperor’s Palace soars,
Stone chambers and cloudy forests store thunder and rain.
I, too, sought the mountains and built a thatched hut,
The Pi-pa Peaks gleaming like jade.
I have heard the Great Elixir must be sought early,
Once refined, its radiance fills the void like a candle.
Dongting and Pengli’s waves surge dark and deep,
The Yellow Crane has departed—where does it fly?
Mercury and lead’s inversion is no trifling matter,
For me, it dissects the essence of heaven and earth.
Who says the Grotto-Heavens hold other scriptures?
The heaven within the grotto is but emptiness.
It is neither the August One’s brush, broad as ten feet,
Nor the Primordial Beginning’s discourse on the suspended pearl.
I trouble you to strike the moth-eaten wood and ask:
Will you gather the dark and return the Great Clod to its origin?

---

**Inscribed on *True Person of Square Gourd Peak’s* Painting *Snow Clearing at Strange Peaks***

Min and E’s primordial snow,
Atop Kunlun’s peak through ten thousand kalpas.
The Gourd Immortal’s ink splashes all with ice and jade,
Sword Pass and Ruan’s cliffs pierce the westernmost sky.
Layered peaks surge like waves—how wondrous and strange!
Warmth stirs the fish and dragons, splitting Xiang River’s flow.
The clearing light first parts the Qin and Duan Bridge,
Pine billows sweep past the moon over Mount Emei.
The old house by the blue river, the mountain’s seclusion,
The farthest shore’s shadowed cliffs turn the frozen stream.
Yuan An’s door and lane lie three feet deep in white,
Ancient trees blaze like coral hooks.
Laughing at my frail self, lying in hills and gullies,
Jade trees and jasper blossoms shroud the misty wastes.
In the great marsh, heavy furs sink in deep frost and sleet,
Spring’s breath gradually turns the plum’s fragrant buds.
Weary, I lay down my brush,
Unrolling this scroll, my heart stirs in wonder.
The lingering inspiration of Wangchuan—distant, yet pursued,
Silently facing the solitary light, I vanish into the boundless.

**Inscription on the *Pine Shade Imparting the Dao* Painting**

At Wei Ridge, the immortal builds his hut east of the jasper grove,
The cloud-nesting Daoist paints a hundred-foot pine.
Before the Hall of Seeing Mountains, its shade spreads like a lofty canopy,
Roots coil round ironstone, branches coil like dragons.
He claims the ancient immortal of Mud-Pellet Peak
Once sought the Dao on Jasper Mountain.
Like the sacred altar where swallows peck white stone,
Long vines and autumn reeds hum with the wind.
Above, it grazes the Nine Heavens’ scattered Silver River,
Below, it links the Three Mountains’ distant starry rainbow.
The Dao of Mud-Pellet Peak surveys boundless kalpas,
Peerless in verdant grandeur, gazing into primordial chaos.

Long ago, the immortal rode a crane over the ridge,
Playing his flute across Min Sea to visit famed peaks.
My old friend, honored as a father,
Returns like a gull to Plum Blossom Pavilion by the creek.
Jia Ding’s mighty words tempered like steel,
His tender whispers deep as Dongfang Shuo’s wit.
The literary splendor of Daoist mountains—how desolate!
With wings outspread, he soars beyond whale’s horn.

I recall mooring my boat by the stream,
Coarse wine beneath pine shade, the creek moon full.
Scales of fish dart through empty green,
Zither notes drift through twilight mist.
Towering trees and sparse bamboos defy depiction,
Stroking the present, mourning the past, my heart drifts.
Bi Hong and Wei Yan were called unmatched,
Yet only the Gourd Immortal’s brush nears their fragrance.
Cloud-descendants should strive to inherit this fame,
Amid turquoise waters and forest peaks in evening’s chill.
This frost-enduring timber, fit for beams and pillars,
Rarely chosen from shadowed cliffs and snowy crags.
Laughing, I sing amid orchid and thoroughwort,
Longing to pluck pine blossoms to brew spring’s nectar.
Raising my head, I summon the two old immortals, Chen and Bai,
Drunk beyond the clouds, playing with autumn’s hues.

---

**Inscription on the *Celestial Palm of Mount Hua* Painting**

Great Hua Peak, anciently named the Sacred Mountain,
Its primordial darkness and earthly might shape solid stone.
Roots thrust west to towering Song and Tai,
Ten-thousand-zhang blue cliffs lean into the void.
Slanted like a half-moon, its palm gleams bright,
Hanging the Silver River from the azure sky.
Touching the heavens, its snowy ridges stretch like a screen,
Piled high, the clustered peaks rival Liang and Huo.
The Son of Heaven’s tours have graced it many times,
Ancient shrines and halls stand a thousand *xun* tall.
Broken bridges stretch to quiet islets,
Old trees bow low over deep streams.
Floating clouds seem to veil evening’s bells and drums,
Iron chains hang high through misty haze.

Here dwells the immortal Wang Ziqiao,
Tigers and leopards guard his stone door.
In our dynasty’s prosperous reign, rites are grand,
We dispatch feathered messengers to convey sincerity.
The jade altar’s ascent is too sacred to attempt,
Returning, I hasten to the Golden Gate to report to the throne.
His mighty words and wondrous carvings illuminate the ages,
Qin and Han vainly boast of Feng and Shan.
Mountain spirits and river lords descend with auspicious signs,
The ancestral altars stand firm, the celestial realm secure.
The Giant Spirit split stone to channel the river,
Bright stars and Jade Maidens dwell on cinnabar mounds.
The Yellow River’s whirlpools rise from the sky’s edge,
The White Emperor’s golden essence glows all around.
The carriage’s axle and arrow’s shaft pave the path to heaven,
I long to follow it and speak with the gods.
I would summon Ma and Wei to ride deer aloft,
But where are the verdant cliffs and cinnabar valleys?
Staff in hand, I laugh and clap Hong Ya’s shoulder,
Hungry, I feast on fallen geese and rosy clouds,
Thirsty, I drink from the Jade Well’s lotus.
If I meet one with purple robes and crimson temples,
I’ll borrow his tea-dragon to soar and return.
The Gourd Immortal, white-haired, marvels at the painting’s perfection,
How could Nie’s and Shu’s traces ever fade?
A single breath of cool wind spans ninety thousand leagues—
Why need I get drunk beneath Emei’s moon?

---

**Seven-Character Quatrains**

**On the *Immortal’s Intent of Square Gourd* Painting**
Weary of rouge and powder marring autumn’s face,
I wash the wind’s dust from one or two peaks.
To know the immortals’ flavorless realm,
Cast off worldly grime and sit beneath the pines.

**The Withered Tree of the True Man of the Western Realm**
Evening sun at the ferry, water merges with sky,
Fallen leaves, cold crows on the ancient road.
My brush races with autumn’s endless sounds—
Where does the fishing rod stand in the western wind?

**Secluded Dwelling in Cloudy Gorges**
Emerald cliffs, cinnabar gorges, clouds over a thousand acres,
A small thatched hut barely contains the seclusion.
I hear that by the sunny window where books are spread,
Wisteria flowers and autumn wind bring flying rain.

**Bamboo Leaves of Square Gourd’s Immortal Crag**
Returning by wild boat, sated with wonders,
In my sleeve, a green jade memento of that time.
Immortal dwellings often lie in azure emptiness—
They show the world only half a branch.

**Gazing at Immortals Pavilion**
Immortals tread the earth, following sacred traces,
Gazing back at simurghs and phoenixes through layered peaks.
Do not say the numinous terrace is untraceable—
Here in Jiangnan stands the highest summit.

**Refining Cinnabar Cliff**
Mercury and lead refined into golden sand,
Moss-covered cliffs and shoulders become home.
Gazing afar at the white clouds’ window,
I still long for the Great Return’s immortal sprouts.

**Cloudy Grotto**
Hollowed stone grottoes where clouds and mist drift,
Sacred herbs and black mushrooms—how many years old?
Sitting, I listen to wind and thunder rise beneath my feet,
Suspecting beyond this, there is no heaven.

**Dragon Pool**
A sheer torrent embraces the rocky shore,
A pool of cold green guards its mossy robe.
The coiled dragon lurks deep in the mountain’s foot,
Once it rode cloud-glue to return as rain.

**Scholar’s Pavilion**
This splendid hall once birthed jade-hall immortals,
Its literary brilliance and radiance illuminate the purple mystery.
Scattered among mortals like countless pearls,
The soaring whale’s legacy stirs a thousand years.

**Star-Worshipping Altar**
Standing tall on the first peak of empty azure,
With flying steps, I mount the wind.
Touching the summit, I forget heaven’s vastness,
Pointing and gesturing amid the night’s vital breath.

**Jade Court Lodge**
Ten-thousand-*ren* cinnabar light illuminates the pearl,
In the open court, I sit serenely like a jade lotus.
Mortals vainly worship the realm of luminous clarity—
Simurghs and cranes wheel in the sky, listening to the *Step Void*.

**Star-Plucking Pavilion**
A lofty pavilion crowns the emerald haze,
Stars are plucked, clad only in five-zhu robes.
Washing the void, the silver desert leaves no autumn trace,
At night, jade pipes and cranes return aloft.

**Gazing at the Numinous Mountain**
Jade-carved hibiscus gleams in the gaze,
Crystal sprouts grow, all imbued with immortal spirit.
When shall I learn to shear Wu Song’s waters,
And cut a single green leaf from Lotus Peak?

**Osmanthus in the Moon**
Golden grains’ autumn fragrance at the moon’s half-branch,
Gladly sharing its pure shadow in the melting ice.
If this body dwelt in the realm of pure emptiness,
No need to wait for cloud-coiffed magpies to cross the bridge.

**Cloud Wilderness Painting**
Gazing afar at the world’s toil on the vast desert’s edge,
Midair, the sound of cranes and pipes drifts in stillness.
Once I grasped the stringless intent,
Not only pine nests—all is white clouds.

**Chess Peak**
Fortunate to tread the high cliff, meeting Spring Peak,
Stone altars and clouds veil east and west.
Immortal chess differs from Shang Mountain’s game—
All lies within the River Chart’s doubled numbers.

**Washing-the-Eyes Pool**
Eyes sweep all peaks, yet weeds choke narrow vales—
Crane-robes, soiled and frayed, bear no mere dust.
How fine to rinse a kalpa’s worldly grime
With but half a cup of heaven’s ladled water.

**Lyric to "Spring in the Qin Garden" · Ascending the True**
From primal chaos’ murky dawn,
Before the limitless, ere time began,
When yin and yang first cleft the void,
And heaven-earth took fixed abode,
Through cycles of stillness and motion,
The True Lord dwelt at the center.
A single spark of numinous brightness
Shone through heaven, illumined earth—
One day, the ancient circle fused,
Wisdom and folly both transcended.
Worldly ties now severed,
Behold the jade-green pool’s mirror,
The moon-polished pearl of the heart.

The eight wastes shine boundless, no corner hid,
Through endless night, the ice-jade nectar melts.
True lead meets mercury, Kan and Li unite,
Fire-dragon and water-tiger, the white key breathes.
White snow congeals the chariot,
Yellow sprouts fill the crucible,
Thunder shakes Kunlun, piercing the Great Void.
When merit is complete,
Await the embryo’s perfection, spirit’s transformation,
Then together ascend heaven’s thoroughfare.

**Lyric to "Water Tune" #1 · Dharma Sea**
Before symbols arose in the primordial,
Ere father and mother were born,
Before time itself—
A single truth stood revealed,
Its radiance ancient, the wellspring of spirit.
Though yin and yang churn within,
Though the five phases invert and cluster,
Vast qi nurtures the Three Fields.
Where its function unleashes killing force,
Thunder and lightning shake the boundless.

Neither mind, nor dharma,
Nor even Chan—
Subtle, wondrous, profound,
A thousand gold coins would not buy its transmission.
Do not cling to talismans or incantations,
But directly awaken to the Mysterious Pass’s patriarch,
Whose fullness lies in your own perfected spirit.
Tiles and thatch, reeds and grasses—
All serve the world yet transcend it.

**Lyric to "Wind Through Pines" · Inquiry into Learning**
Ten years of lamp-shadowed nights, my constant companion,
Cold and heat alternating, hastening time.
How often I laid down the rhinoceros-horn brush by the narrow window,
Pored over tattered scrolls—who else savored their flavor?
Beyond the curtain, snow deepens, wind tightens,
Yet plum blossoms thrive, and the muse of poetry stirs.

A thousand classics, ten thousand histories suffice for governance,
Yet my scholarly ambition grows ever more vast.
I question the Heavenly Root and Moon Grotto,
Pondering the affairs of ancient and modern literature—
How many have lost their way at the ford?
Gather in the luminous clarity of the empty spirit,
And wherever you lean on your blossom staff, spring follows.
Free of vulgar thoughts—
Contemplate and investigate.

**Contemplating the Mundane**
Beneath Misty Lake Peak,
I wove a nest of pines and clouds,
Forgetting dawn and dusk in motion.
The floating world’s endless rise and fall—
A laugh, and it scatters like duckweed in a dream.
Green bamboo and yellow blossoms,
The sound of water lending color—
Who knows this flavor’s depth?
Limpid and bright,
Form and emptiness both self-evident.

Sky’s light and cloud’s shadows drift,
Painting the long expanse of azure,
A mirror-clear pool.
Spring departs, autumn arrives, yet the heart remains at ease,
Entrusted to the wild’s fish and crows.
Seas vast, rivers calm,
Moon bright, wind gentle,
Pure pipes’ notes fade into silence.
Then stride forth to the azure waves,
Reciting aloud beneath heaven’s canopy.

**Lyric to "Water Tune" · Inner Work**
The supreme Dao speaks no words,
In silence, it guards the compass’s center.
Vast and obscure, it circulates through the unseen,
A single darkness animating the primal palace.
Gathering metal’s essence and wood’s sap,
True earth captures lead and mercury within—
In an instant, divine power manifests.
Measuring the trigrams, sounding the key,
Thunder and wind roar.
Kan and Li invert,
Fire soars over the azure sea, refining true emptiness.
The Great One embraces true form,
The jade crucible’s flowing pearls congeal,
Spirit and transformation merge with the mysterious.
Return to Penglai’s isles,
Through kalpas vast, play in the primordial chaos.

**Lyric to "Court Full of Fragrance" · Mountain Dwelling**
I cast aside my raven-black staff,
Sought a thatched hut—
Who knew it would be but remnant streams and broken hills?
I dug a pond, planted trees,
Plum and bamboo left to twine freely.
Sweet grasses and idle blossoms carpet the earth,
Mist and rosy clouds enfold the mossy path and wicker gate.
No one comes—
Spring winds and autumn moons,
Pines and chrysanthemums keep me company in quiet murmurs.

With bowl and gourd, I live as fate allows,
No glory, no shame,
Along woodcutter’s paths and fisherman’s bays.
With forest apes and valley crows,
I share evening’s joy and morning’s delight.
Sweeping away the dust of passion and karmic grime,
I don my robe, sit in true breath,
Nurturing the returning elixir.
In leisurely ease,
A lone zither, a single crane—
Frost and dew leave no mark on my face.

**Lyric to "Su Wu the Slow" · Leisure’s Dissolution**
Awakening to illusion, seeking truth,
I vowed for years to transcend birth and death.
Through wind-sifted snow, I compiled texts,
Reading by night, chanting by day,
Probing the wisdom of sages past and present.
Dao’s mystery, Chan’s lineage—
Ten thousand differences, one root.
To discern what lies beyond scrutiny,
This boundless, unobstructed true emptiness,
Not even the moon’s waxing and waning affects it.

How laughable—
A bamboo chair, a thin meditation mat,
A pine-framed window, an osmanthus casement,
Each step a stride toward loftiness.
Yet the world’s dust I shun,
Water and clouds my companions,
Reclining in my old garden amid wind and snow.
Fine steeds and sable robes,
Jade sleeves and rouge shells—
All fleeting splendor, idle talk.
Turn swiftly—here is the shore,
Curtains part to reveal light,
The moon of the mind, the heaven of nature.

**Lyric to "All Crimson" · Worldly Observations**
I recall my youth,
Where once I sought pleasure—
All now changed, no trace remains.
I listen to the sea’s swelling tide,
The brocade of waves receding,
The four cities’ eternal spring.
At the song-and-dance tower, I loathed the setting sun,
Amid pipes and strings, I raged at drunken oblivion.
Behold the present—
How many moments of glory and withering?
Sorrow defies order.

Dream’s phantoms wake,
Worldly cares disperse—
Vain sighs, empty warnings.
I lament the orchid oar, the reed pavilion,
The cold water’s misty tinkling.
No share in rivers and lakes’s frayed ends,
Yet heaven’s heart-moon casts its reflection in the limpid pool.
Reflecting on this floating life,
I see through joy and sorrow—
The river’s waves grow still.

**Lyric to "Drunken River Moon" · Rivers and Lakes**
Once I followed a fishing skiff,
Played with autumn’s waves,
Witnessing rivers and lakes’ vast expanse.
Beyond the two shores’ white caltrop isles,
Dew glistened on reeds, maple leaves fell.
Midnight’s tide roared,
Midheaven’s moon shone,
The plum-blossom horn turned again.
Pushing open the hatch, I asked—
Where were my old friends? Everywhere, desolation.

I launched the oars at Shepherd’s Shore, the fishing village,
By the city’s edge at dusk,
Returning crows cried in flocks.
Green wine, yellow blossoms,
Amid mist and rain—
How many dreams of my old garden’s groves and vales?
The crumbling pagoda’s wind howled,
Sea gates and mountains shrank,
Spring’s end, willows draped the outer walls.
Returning to the grove,
I shook my robes, gazed loftily at the boundless.

**Lyric to "Gazing at Plum Blossoms" · Illusory Bonds**
This floating world knows no bounds,
Its dusty burdens seen through—
How long can illusion last?
Through kalpas of enmity and kinship,
Lifetimes of acquaintance,
Thin as a wisp of cloud, this affection.
In vain I boast of cunning schemes,
Parading heroism—
Only adding to karmic shadows.

All schemes and stratagems exhausted,
Chasing fame and profit through right and wrong.
Creation is impartial—
Yet the spirit’s terrace dims itself,
Sinking in the burning sea of suffering.
Cast it all away:
Wild waters, sparse woods, no trace of passage,
Moon bright, wind gentle.

**Lyric to "Unraveling Red" · Awakening**
The true nature of the original self is empty as space,
Its narrow bounds dissolved, round clarity revealed.
Passions’ dust obscures the heart-pearl’s light,
Drowning in the deep abyss—
Yet the spirit’s radiance never fades,
A single gleam of brilliance, never far.
Sweep away the floating clouds,
All phenomena unobstructed,
The heart of heaven appears.

Wildflowers, crying crows—asking amidst ease,
Spring gazes upon seas and mulberry fields,
How many shallows and depths?
Flourishing and decay alternate in constant flux,
All sorrows of mountains and bitter seas,
Wandering, hard to turn back.
Suddenly awakened—
Heaven and earth hold wondrous mystery.
By the pine and bamboo,
In quiet solitude, trace the true source.
At Caoxi’s crossroads, no shadowed trees,
Neither dharma nor Chan.
Only when the yang within Kan arises,
Light surges like rolling waves.

Who grasps stillness, drinks the elixir,
Dispels floating cares?
Seeing without form,
Hearing without sound,
Speaking without distinction.
This carefree, drifting life—truly enviable,
Nestled in white clouds’ embrace, cradling folly and weariness.
With cold springs and withered trees,
Dimly glimpsed, the pot of heaven.

**Lyric to "Wind Through Pines"**
In Jiangcheng, drowned in sickly wine, hard to savor,
Thin temples startle at morning’s hairpin.
Summer’s heat gone, autumn’s light already narrow,
Red dust far, the slanting sun turns sticky.
Orchid curtains hold lingering night’s traces,
Clear frost still dampens spring robes.
On Qinhuai, the tide settles, jade-green,
Returning swallows rest, murmuring.
White clouds’ curtains and drapes grow cold too soon—
Who now asks of crow-script or fish-letters?
Soon, the sound of oars returning,
Yellow blossoms, white wine, south of the village.

*End of Volume Twelve of Jianquan Collection*
*(Note: The original tune title was mistakenly given as "Water Dragon Chant")*
